Table 3.1b: Work packages description  
 
Objectives  
• To perform an updated review of the technical literature with attention to patents dealing with the target 
products and processes  
• To define specifications for the materials & processes for bio-based food-contact material (FCM)  
• To define specifications for the materials & processes to upcycle SRM via tailored PRESERVE approaches 
Description of work  
Task 1.1 Updated review of the state-of-the-art 
Leader: ASU-Partners involved: each partner will provide respectively scientific or industrial information relevant to 
his field 
An up -to-date review of scientific literature (peer reviewed journals and magazines), patents and company 
brochures will be carried out to ensure that all relevant research in the area is identified and that any 
developments since proposal preparation stage are included. This task will complement and update the State-of-
the-Art presented in Section 1.4 and  will map any competitive commercial approaches. This will also include a 
market survey and benchmarking of existing solutions and in development state. Special focus will be given to bio-
based plastics and their improvements routes in terms barrier properties, use of coatings, graftings, etc. as well as 
conversion processes and EoL options including biodegradation, upcycling, etc. Furthermore, the current offer and 
gaps in recycled biopolymers will be particularly surveyed. The results of this task will feed into review paper(s) 
that will be published in open access scientific journals of high reputation. 
Task 1.2 Specifications of target bio-based packaging for food contact 
Leader: EUBP-Partners involved: ASU, AIMPLAS, CTB, UNIBO, CARB, SUDPACK, GPI, DANONE, MDLZ, ITENE, IRIS, 
PLANET, ROMEI 
Materials specifications will be defined for each food -associated packaging application preselected in table 1. 4 
(defining in fu rther details the demonstrators’ requirements and types for packing dairy pro ducts, drinks and 
snacks) based on the participating packaging manufacturers’ as well as end users’ expertise and the properties of 
the materials currently used that will be consi dered as benchmarks. Other specific market requirements for the 
implementation of new materials will be defined (e.g. cost, regu latory / conformity and environmental aspects, 
processability, as well as ability to sort and recycle each packaging type, etc.). The available processes along the 
value chain of research and industrial partners will be mapped to support a smooth transfer of the results between 
WP2-3 and 5. In link with WP6, the safe by design (SdD) approach will be applied to the materials selecte d for 
further research in the following WPs. Initial knowledge on consumer acceptance of bio -packaging will be 
considered by ASU in link with WP7. 
Task 1.3. Specifications of target recycled bio-based packaging and other recovered polymers applications 
Leader: EUBP- Partners involved: ASU, AIMPLAS, CTB, UNIBO, CARB, SUDPACK, SIBO, BDF, DENIMX, IRIS, PLANET, 
SILON 
Materials specifications will be defined for each SRM application preselected in table 1.4 targeted to be obtained 
from recovered food packaging materials (defining in further details the demonstrators’ requirements and types 
for packing personal care products, for bags and for composites) based on the properties of the materials currently 
used that will be considered as benchmarks. Other specific m arket requirements for the implementation of new 
materials will be defined (e.g. tolerance to impurities r esulting from the recovery step, cost, regulatory / 
conformity and environmental aspects, processability, as well as ability to sort and recycle each packaging type, 
etc.). The available SRM processing capabilities along the value chain of research and ind ustrial partners will be 
mapped to support a smooth transfer of the results between WP2 -3 and 5. Moreover, the general consumers’ 
acceptance of upcycled polymers for packaging applications will be initially assessed by ASU in link with WP7.

D1.3 Specifications of target recycled bio -based packaging and other recovered polymers applications  (M4) - 
written report including target properties, processing, processing and EoL aspects linked to task 1.3 
 
 
Objectives  
• To optimize the fermentation process of mcl-PHAs in order to increase their hydrophobicity.   
• To optimize the formulation of water-based and solvent based PHA coatings with enhanced water vapour 
barrier properties.  
• To fine tune protein coatings and adhesives for new multilayer structures with delamination potential.  
• To optimize coatings to avoid microfibre release from upcycled materials. 
• To improve the mechanical and barrier properties of biopolymers with eBeam treatment.  
Description of work  
For the tasks in this WP, commercially available bio-PE, bio-PET, moulded pulp trays will be sourced according to 
WP1 specifications, BO -PLA films will be provided by SUDPACK and different tailored paper and board will be 
provided by GPI for coatings/ adhesives application trials whereas the partners involved in developing the EoL 
solutions for delaminating the developed coating will follow the inputs for WP4 (ROMEI, PLATO). 
 
Task 2.1. Development and processing of barrier protein coatings 
Subtask 2.1.1. Coating Optimization and upscale of protein coatings to the project targets- Leader: ASU   Partners 
involved: IVV 
Based on prior developments, aqueous protein -based coating formulations will be optimized regarding their 
barrier and mechanical properties and tailored for target paper and polymer substrates. Commercially available 
whey protein with high performance and purity will be used. The protein dry matter in the formulation is typically 
between 5 and 20 % (w/w). Thermal treatments such as denaturatio n to make functional groups available for 
cross-linking will be considered during the drying process or as a preliminary step. Adequate amounts and nature 
of plasticisers will be mixed to obtain the desired properties.  
Coatings application trials after surface activation by corona treatment of polymer substrates will be initially done 
using a lab scale coating automat (CUF 5 Sumet Messtechnik). Thereby coating parameters will be varied and 
optimized (e.g. temperature of the formulation, wet coating weight, coating speed as well as drying temperature 
and time). The coated sheets will be characterized regarding the relevant properties such as flexibility, mechanical 
stability and barrier properties (OTR, WVTR). The availability of surface functional groups (e .g. hydroxyl-, amino- 
and thiol-groups), which are necessary for maintaining adhesive forces in the foreseen laminat ion step (subtask 
2.3.1 and 2.5.3), will be monitored by FTIR, Raman and fluorescence spectroscopy of isocyanate -linked 
fluorophores. Following the requirements defined in WP1, this subtask also includes iteratively adjustments of the 
formulation / process in compliance with the envisaged demonstrators to ensure scalability.  
Subtask 2.1.2. Grafting with fatty acids to improve water vapour barrier- Leader: ASU   Partners involved: SUDPACK 
To obtain water vapour barrier appropriate for the envisaged demonstrators, FA grafting will be performed at lab 
scale by ASU. Pre-existing formulas developed in past and ongoing projects will be further optimized for application 
on the intended (coated) bio -based polymer films . This includes adjusting the formulas where needed to the 
polymer substrate, e.g. PLA, protein coatings etc., and optimiz ing the grafting process itself. Subsequently the 
water vapour barrier as well as the oxygen barrier will be analysed  as well as liquid repellency to determine the 
potential to generate possible easy emptying effects to reduce product wastes in the package. The most promising 
formula will then be selected for the subsequent tasks and upscaling at SUDPACK in WP5. 
Subtask 2.1.3 Metallization of protein-based coatings- Leader: IVV    Partners involved: ASU 
Inorganic barrier layers are used to improve the barrier properties of protein coatings (OTR < 1 cm 3 /m2 d bar, 
WVTR < 1 g /m 2 d). Where needed, planarization layers to smoothen the substrate surface will be applied. The 
process is divided in i) drying to <2.5% water content; ii) physical vapour deposition (PVD); iii) equilibration at 50% 
RH to maintain protein plasticity.  Inorganic barriers are very thin metals (Al) or metal oxides (Al 2O3, SiOx) layers 
with thicknesses down to 80 nm. They will be deposited by eBeam evaporation in a high vacuum chamber in a roll-
to-roll process (coating width ~30 cm). Inorganic barrier layers will be characterized regarding permeability (OTR, 
WVTR), surface morphology, layer homogeneity and thickness (electron microscopy, AFM).

Task 2.2. Development and processing of water barrier PHA coatings 
Subtask 2.2.1. Optimization of the PHA fermentation process - Leader: BIOPOL    Partners involved: AIMPLAS 
The objective of this subtask is to provide enough PHA material for the PHA coatings in the subsequent subtask. 
We will take advantage of modified strains and fermentation processes developed in  the previous REFUCOAT 
project, adapting the processes based on the feedback from subtask 2.2.2. 
Synthesis of PHA modified with lipids groups in order to increase the PHAs hydr ophobicity. The different 
production pathways of the selected Pseudomonas and ot her bacterial strains will be exploited. The main 
monomer in this case will be 3-hydroxydecanoate, but 3-hydroxy-5-dodecenoate and 3-hydroxy-7-tetradecenoate 
will also be produ ced. When lipids are employed, the mcl -PHA is produced through the β-oxidation pathway. In 
this case, the structure of the precursor is recovered in the resulting mcl -PHA. In order to obtain higher 
hydrophobicity in the mcl -PHA, mutants of Pseudomonas strains in the β-oxidation pathway will be employed. 
Other functionalities will be obtained by combination of substrates and modified strains. A range of different 
modified mcl-PHA will be obtained and their composition will be analyzed by GC-FID and GC-MS.  
Down-stream process. Isolation and purification procedures will be a pplied: biomass concentration, cell 
disruption, polymer extraction and polymer precipitation, will be developed initially in lab scale trials by using low 
toxicity bio-based solvents that c an be recycled during several cycles. The molecular weight and poly dispersity 
index will be analyzed by GPC.  
Scale-up production. Based on previous developments, the fermentation and downstream processes will be 
scaled-up to 300-L with the most promising polymer. At least 10 kgs of PHA will be delivered to subtask 2.2.2. 
Subtask 2.2.2. Optimization of the PHA water vapour barrier coatings formulation - Leader: AIMPLAS - Partners 
involved: CTB, BIOPOL, BOSTIK 
In this task, the optimization of formulation of the PHA coating will be carried out following two different strategies 
based on ongoing projects: solvent -based formulations by AIMPLAS and recently patented plastisol technology 
(solvent free) by CTB. Both formulations will be optimized to reach the specific project target defined in WP1 to 
obtain minimal water vapour pe rmeability and an increased durability. This can be achieved by increasing the 
crystallinity with nucleating agents, adding hydrophobicity w ith different additives (fatty acids, waxes) and by 
crosslinking the PHA. Both conventional food contact approved crosslinkers, such as polymeric carbodiimides and 
polyisocyanates as well as novel biobased crosslinkers based on starch aldehydes, citric acid or itaconic anhydrides 
will be investigated. PHA modifications with bio -based 10 -undecenoic acid that could provid e antimicrobial 
properties from BOSTIK will be studied as well. Also, a variety of plasticisers will be tested as they can heavily 
influence the biodegradation, flexibility and durability of the coatings. Additives will also be added to the 
formulation to provide specific characteristics and adequate conditions for the drying process, as well as to 
improve the printing quality on the polymer substrate or the compatibility with the protein coatings and adhesives 
developed in tasks 2.1 and 2.3. Substrate pre-treatment with corona or plasma will be considered to improve the 
printability.  
The different coatings obtained with both strategies will be printed at lab -scale at different application weights. 
Parameters like drying temperature and time will be iterati vely modified to get the correct evaporation of the 
solvent. The quality of the printed samples will be validated by adhesion and abrasion tests according to ISO 2409 
and ISO 105 -X12 respectively. Furthermore, the WVTR and OTR will be measured. The obtaine d values will be 
decisive for the selection of the appropriate grammage to apply,  as well as in selecting the most suitable 
formulations for the different demonstrators in WP5. Cobb tests for liquid and grease resistance will be also 
performed following the requirements defined in WP1. Subsequently, printing tests will be carried out a t the 
laboratory level of the selected formulations using different coating methodologies depending on the process 
requirements defined in WP1 for the final demonstrators (fle xography, dip -coating, gravure -coating, slot-die 
coating, spray-coating, etc.). The application parameters and the viscosity will be optimized.  
   
Task 2.3. Development and processing of bio-based adhesives  
Subtask 2.3.1. Polyurethane wet -chemical coating adhesives - Leader: BOSTIK (Arkema), Partners involved: IVV, 
UNIBO 
The wet- chemical adhesives will be developed for laminat ing substrates, which are already coated with protein 
barrier coating or primer in Task 2.5.1 (so called face-to-face lamination). The adhesives will be polyurethane (PU) 
based. Their application process will be by means of gravure, reverse-roll or kiss-coating process. Covalent bonds 
with the protein functional groups will be formed with developed isocyanate-functionalized pre-polymers. A high 
availability of isocyanate groups in the branched pre -polymer is k ey to maintain strong adhesion to the protein 
coatings. The prepolymer backbone will originate from >50% biobased monomers (e.g. vegetable oil polyols) and 
will be developed by polycondensation during a non-aqueous process. 
Oligomers obtained via enzymatic recycling in task 4.4 and modified with specific functional groups will also be 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 42 of 70 
investigated as prepolymer source. The amount of partly bio-based adhesive used for lamination is generally low 
(dry layer thickness ~3g/m 2 substrate) allowing meeting the target bio-content for the laminated. Adhesives will 
be characterized by SEC-GPC, FTIR and possibly NMR where necessary. Initial lamination tests with coatings from 
subtask 2.1.1 will be performed and laminate bond strength will be measured according to standards used by the 
flexible packaging industry (e.g. T-peel-test ASTM D 1876 / DIN 55529 ) according to the specifications defined in 
WP1. A typical strength of 4 N / 15 mm is expec ted to be achievable. Based on these results , at least one 
formulation will be selected, upscaled (>10 L) and tested on the roll-to-roll coating pilot plant at IVV in WP 2.5. 
Subtask 2.3.2. Hot melt adhesives - Leader: IVV -Partners involved: BOSTIK, UNIBO 
A biodegradable hot melt adhesive based on casein will be developed by IVV for lamination of polymeric tray 
sheets (for further thermoforming) and as planarization layer on paper/cardboard substrates. Casein powder will 
be compounded using a co -rotating t win screw extruder (Dr. Collin, 24 D, 25 mm diameter) with selected 
plasticizers (20-80% of water, glycerol, urea, other sugar alcohols, PEG,  …) or further plant -based proteins (e.g. 
soy or sunflower). Oligomers obtained in task 4.4, and, if necessary, che mically modified, will also be tested for 
their use as plasticizers for adhesive formulations. The melt processing temperature of the plasticized protein 
mixture is typically at ~ 80-120°C, which should be below the substrate melting temperature and below the protein 
degradation temperature. Produced compounds will be characterized thermally ( by DSC) and mechanically 
(Young’s modulus, tensile strength, elongation at break).  
   
Task 2.4. Surface treatments.  
Subtask 2.4.1. Optimization of the formulation of Functional Finishing treatment to reduce microplastics -Leader: 
ITENE - Partners involved: UNIBO, IRIS, CTB 
Our target is to provide a functional coating for the durable textile SRM applications showing long-term durability 
and high-performance even after several washings, thus avoiding the microfibre release/detachment. Different 
chemical compounds and polymers, specifically the upcycled polyesters produced in task 4.4 will be evaluated as 
solutions improving the abrasion resistance and avoiding fibre breakage. Lab scale reactors and mixing equipment 
will be used to optimally formulate the finish or coating. This development will be performed at laboratory scale 
using different techniques previous to upscaling.  
A preliminary stage to determine the coating effectiveness will be to determine the level of microplastics and/or 
nanoplastics release during the intended conditions of use for  standard uncoated upcycled non-woven fabrics 
provided by SILON. To test both coated and uncoated fabrics, two main approaches will be followed: a) washing 
trials (based on ISO 105 -C06:2010) evaluating released fibres, and b) mesocosm (internally developed 
methodology by ITENE) studies in freshwater and marine water to simulate a direct release into the environment, 
with either a continuous point-source discharge, and accidental discharge. In both cases, several physico-chemical 
analyses will be performed to assess release, morphology of particles, using scanning electron microscopy (SEM) 
for samples collected in filters and Dynamic light scattering (DLS) (UNIBO) for water samples. Further studies using 
FTIR, Raman,  and eventually X -ray photoelectron (XPS) characterization will be conducted to have a better 
understanding of the composition of released fibers and particles. IRIS will also apply high resolution hyperspectral 
imaging as a fast detection method to determine the size and composition of the released microplastics. 
Subtask 2.4.2. eBeam treatment to improve surface properties- Leader: ASU -  Partners involved: NTT 
Selected materials, e.g. protein coated and FA-grafted bio-based polymer films or coated textiles from tasks 2.1-
2.4.1, will be irradiated by electron beam (eBeam) treatment at lab scale by ASU in order to further impr ove the 
mechanical and barrier properties or stability by crosslinking. As electron irradiation can induce both crosslinking 
and chain scission, the process parameters such as dose, voltage and atmosphere will be iteratively chosen to 
ensure crosslinking a s dominant eBeam effect. Irradiated films wil l then be analysed regarding mechanical and 
barrier properties (WVP, OTR) at ASU and compared to the untreated samples by the material provider. Hygienic 
and/ or antimicrobial effects in presence of selected add itives will also be checked. Treated materials will be 
provided to WP4 to ascertain the effect on the materials reprocessability. Furthermore, where relevant, the effect 
of eBeam regarding the release of microplastic will be analysed by ITENE in the previo us subtask . The most 
promising results and process parameters will then feed in Task 2.5 and WP5. 
   
Task 2.5. Development and characterization of multilayer structures  
Subtask 2.5.1. Coatings application and characterization of the coated film - Leader: AIMPLAS-  Partners involved: 
ASU, IVV 
The formulation of the different coatings (protein and PHA) as well as the adhesives will be upscaled and applied 
on different substrates at pilot plant scale to test their lamination and further convertibility where required.  
Regarding the formulation of PHA, two formulations, one for each strategy, will be selected to be upscaled based 
on the characterization results obtained in Task 2.2. Batches of up to 30 L will be obtained in 50 L glass reactors. 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 43 of 70 
Once prepared, the coating will be applied at pilot scale usin g different printing technologies depending on the 
defined demonstrators. At least 100 m of PHA -coated films will be produced to check the coating performance. 
Mechanical and barrier properties will be measured at this point. 
Regarding the protein coatings, based on these results obtained in task 2.1.1., at least one formulation per protein 
will be selected and upscaled (3-5 L) for tests on the roll-to-roll coating pilot plant at IVV. The process parameters 
will be iteratively adjusted and optimized in compliance with the envisaged demonstrators to ensure scalability in 
WP5. This includes, inter alia, the analyses of mechanical and barrier properties. FA grafting will be applied when 
needed as indicated in Table 1.4 to reach higher barrier properties and or surface repellence properties. 
Regarding the adhesive formulations, selected adhesive formulations from task 2.3 will be upscaled at BOSTIK (5-
10 kg): the urethane-based crosslinking system that will be applied by means of wet -chemical coating (between 
protein-coated polymer substrates) and the protein -based hot -melt thermoplastic that will be applied by co -
extrusion lamination process (on thermoformable polymer sheets or on cardboard). 
Materials will be provided to WP4 for the biodegradability tests. If th e biodegradation rates are not enough, 
modification on the different formulations will be performed.  
Subtask 2.5.2. Application of a functional fi nishing treatment to reduce microplastics - Leader: ITENE- Partners 
involved: CTB 
On this subtask, processing steps and methodologies considered on subtask 2.4.1 will be upscaled. Jacketed 
reactors with a maximum capacity of 100L will be used to perform required mixing/reaction steps for the selected 
formulations for this task and WP5. CTB will perform application test on different textile substrates on pilot scale 
machines (width 50 cm). Both coating (application with knife coating, transfer coating, …) and finish (dipping and 
full impregnation) technologies will be tested. Characterization tests will be performed based on aforementioned 
2.4.1 tests. 
Subtask 2.5.3. Production and characterization of multilayer structures- Leader: IVV -   Partners involved: BOSTIK, 
AIMPLAS, ASU, IRIS 
Preliminary multilayer structures defined for the initial demonstrators from WP5 wi ll be produced and 
characterized. The focus will be given to the processability of the novel materials coming from Tasks 2.1 to 2.4, 
their machinability, thermoformability w here required, compatibility between the layers, adhesion to the 
substrates, final laminate quality, and barrier performance. For the processes involving new coatings with resulting 
properties highly depending on the homogeneity of the application, IRIS wi ll apply spectral reflectance 
measurements as a support to process optimization. Feedback will be given to Tasks 2.1-2.4 in case improvements 
are needed. The best performing and most applicable formulation and combination thereof in each multilayer 
structure will be identified as input for upscaling in WP5. The wet chemical coating and lamination roll-to-roll pilot 
line at IVV and AIMPLAS will be used for the production of the multilayer structures based on barrier coatings and 
PU adhesives. The thermoplastic hot melt adhesive lamination will be performed using the co-extrusion lamination 
process at IVV (for polymeric substrates) and AIMPLAS (for cardboard substrates).  
The different structures will be characterized in terms of laminate bond strength between the layers, OTR, WVTR, 
as well as regarding sealability, mechanical and optical pr operties in order  to assess whether the required 
properties are met. Where applicable , contact angle measurements will be performed to address repellence 
properties (IVV, AIMPLAS, ASU…). Furthermore, for the tray demonstrators, preliminary thermoforming tests will 
be carried out at IVV. Parameters such as the heating power, heating and cooling time and vacuum will be 
optimized. The best structure obtained w ill be characterized in terms of mechanical and barrier properties to 
evaluate the effect of the process on the properties of the structure.   
Likewise, for cosmetic packaging bottles, preliminary test of injection blow moulding  will be carried out  by 
AIMPLAS. Since the melting temperature of PHA is low and can degrade during processing, a laminated structure 
PLA/PHA/PLA will be obtained first. Next, in-mould labelling labels with the proper geometry and dimensions to 
completely cover the prototype mold will be produced. Parameters such as temperature and air pressure will be 
optimized to ensure good integr ation. For moulded pulp packaging, a similar labelling approach  and/or spray 
coating will be tested. For the spray coating application , different coating techniques such as high-volume low 
pressure and/or airless spraying will be tested depending on the coating materials selected.  
The effect of eBeam will be tested on selected structures (ASU). 
Materials will be provided by M18 to WP4 for EoL analysis and sufficient amount of the different selected coatings 
and adhesives will be available by M24 for WP5.

D2.2. Optimization of PHA fermentation process. (M12) – report on the optimization of the P HA fermentation

coatings of textiles linked to task 2.4. 
D2.6. eBeam Treatment. (M15) report on eBeam treatment of coated/ grafted bio-based material, linked task 2.4. 
D2.7. Production of multilayer structures. (M18) report on the production of multilayer structures according to the 
final demonstrators linked to task 2.5. 
D2.8. Upscaling of coatings and adhesives. (M24) report on the upscaling process of formulation and application 
of coatings and adhesives linked to task 2.5. 
 
 
 
 
Objectives  
• Development of biodegradable PLA and PLA blends in mild conditions by using encapsulated enzyme 
formulations to obtain home compostable biobased materials 
• Set up of eBeam treatment to improve the properties of selected materials and blends 
• Development and characterization of self - and micro fibrillated reinforced biobased materials with 
improved mechanical and barrier properties 
Description of work 
In this WP, core materials and blends will be upcycled improving the material properties by using  enzymes, 
radiation treatment and/or by applying microfibrillar and self -reinforced structures. A stepwise strategy will be 
followed: the research will start at lab scale allowing a fast screening. The most promising routes will be 
investigated at pilot scale, finally resulting in a selection of upcycled materials to be evaluated at semi -industrial 
scale in textiles, packaging and composites in WP5 to be injected or used as substrates for laminates. 
Task 3.1 Development of biodegradable PLA biomaterials using enzymes 
Leader: CARB -Partners involved: OWS, ITENE, CTB (for all subtasks) 
CARB has developed enzymated masterbatches enabling to reach home compost ability for PLA materials and 
packaging, especially when recycling has so far been difficult due to multilayer structure  or soiled packaging. In 
this task , enzymated masterbatches developed by CARB will be introduced in PLA and rPLA to tackle the 
applications where organic recycling may be preferable. 
Subtask 3.1.1 First generation of enzymated biomaterials 
CARB will provide the partners with a first generation of enzymated masterbatch enabling PLA biodegradation in 
home composting conditions. Small scale p lastics materials will be produced in order to evaluate the optimum 
concentration of the enzymated masterbatch that needs to be introduced according to the final materials 
requirements (e.g. thickness). Analytical and screening methods will be used in a fi rst intention to control and 
validate the enzyme activity within the tested compounds.  This first generation of enzymated masterbatch will 
neither be approved for Food Contact by EFSA, nor by FDA and will be thus used either for experimental purpose 
or being used behind a functional barrier, as an exception already approved by the packaging regulations both in 
Europe and in the US. Its application will be also considered for packaging personal care products as well as for 
textiles and transport packaging using SRM from WP4. As such, additional testing will be able to be conducted for 
fiber applications in relation with CTB.  
Subtask 3.1.2 Second generation of enzymated biomaterials 
By M24, CARB will produce a second generation of self -degrading PLA masterbat ch, hav ing enhanced 
thermostability and for which a Food Contact Authorization will have been requested both at European level with 
EFSA but also in the USA. Additional volumes of enzymated masterbatch will be provided for validation on pilot 
lines (or ind ustrial, depending on the application targeted) to enlarge the potential markets to food packaging 
applications which will be validated in WP5.  
The enzymated masterbatches will be provided to WP 4 to test the most effective EoL, including home composting 
and soil biodegradation conditions. After this initial validation, masterbatches will be produced at up to hundred 
kilo scale to be tested on the plastic processing lines of the partners in WP5.

Upcycling of core materials and blends
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 45 of 70 
Task 3.2 Radiation treatment for selected materials and blends 
Leader: ASU - Partners involved: NTT, ITENE 
As tested for the coating in WP2, r adiation treatment will also be applied on the core bio-based packaging 
materials with the aim to improve their barrier properties and me chanical performance. Samples to treat will be 
provided by tasks 3.1 and 3.1. The conditions for eBeam treatment will be iteratively set -up at lab scale by ASU. 
To identify the optimal conditions, a broad range of doses and different atmosphere conditions will be surveyed. 
Optimal conditions defined at lab scale from ASU will then be transferred on the semi-industrial scale available at 
NTT facility. The reliability of the process will be assessed by running the process in continuous mode and by 
defining the final parameters to be implemented a t large scale. The effect of eBeam radiation on the properties 
of biopolymers will be assessed. This will include the characterization of the mechanical and barrier properties 
(WVTR, OTR) as well as determination of degree of crosslinking, colour analyses and contact angle measurements 
at lab scale at ASU. Moreover, radical species generated during the irradiation will be monitored by EPR 
spectroscopy to identify and characterize the recombination mechanism inducing pol ymer chain crosslinking. 
Enzymatic deg radation and reprocessing of samples will be carried out in WP4 to prove that the crosslinked 
polymers is still recyclable mechanically and/or organically. 
Task 3.3 Development and characterization of self- reinforced PLA materials 
Leader: CTB - Partners involved: ASU, AIMPLAS, SILON, SUDPACK 
In this task, PLA materials with both low and high melting temperatures (Tm) will be selected, which will in a next 
step be combined to a self-reinforced composite. The materials will be analysed according to their processability 
in foil (CTB, AIMPLAS) and  textile filament (CTB, SILON) extrusion for corresponding processing conditions, e.g. 
high draw ratios and extruder temperatures of about 200-240°C. This includes preliminary evaluation of the flow 
behaviour via structural and rheological measurements in order to achieve good processing properties, but also 
to reach the mechanical requirements. An evaluation of the potential for extrusion / melt spinning will be done 
using a pilot scale extrusion process. Full characte risation of the produced foils / yarns  will be performed. The 
characterisation tests include mechanical analysis (tensile strength, modulus, elongation at break), determination 
of the materials density (correlated to molecular structure and composition), s hrinkage triggered by heat, and 
resulting shift in mechanical properties, and DSC (crystalline structure, melting temperature).  
After extrusion, the low and high melting foils / filaments will be combined in different structures and transformed 
into self-reinforced thermoformed sheets, foils to be used in injection moulding applications (in mould labelling 
technology in WP2/5 ) or preforms usable for extrusion blowing. A first screening and quality control of the 
produced PLA foils and filaments will be per formed using film stacking and filamen t winding respectively, and 
compression moulding to manufacture unidirectional composite sheets, for mechanical tests and back-calculation 
of the properties of the PLA reinforcement sheets.  Sheets and films will be pr ovided to task 2.5. SILON, with the 
support of CTB and AIMPLAS, will upscale the PLA self -reinforced materials and provide self -reinforced sheets, 
films or textiles to WP5, which quality will be assessed by SUDPACK to ensure further convertibility. 
Task 3.4 Development and characterization of micro fibrillated reinforced materials 
Leader: CTB - Partners involved: ASU, IRIS, ITENE, AIMPLAS, PLANET, SILON (for all subtasks) 
While task 3.3 is focusing on PLA as matrix, other biopolymer matrices such as bio -PE, bio-PET and bio-PA could 
be considered as well. As those materials are typically used for the production of multilayered structures in order 
to reach the desired propert ies, polymer blends and their possibility to form micro -fibrillated structures will be  
considered using virgin materials in this task as a basis for the use as EoL upcycling option for coextruded structures 
in WP4. Only well -chosen polymer pairs have suita ble characteristics so that a fibrillar polymer structure will be 
formed. Three biopol ymer grades will be selected: bio -PET, bio -PA and bio -PE. The bio -PE will be selected as 
reference matrix polymer. As a microfibril forming phase, bio-PET and bio-PA will be chosen. In this task, a selection 
of suitable biobased grades will be made based o n a detailed characterization of rheological behavior (capillary 
and rotational rheometry) and thermal properties (DSC, MDSC and TGA). Based on the results of these tests  and 
the selection rules for microfibril formation, grades that have the potential to form microfibrils will be selected for 
each of the reference polymers. 
Subtask 3.4.1 Compounding trials with integrated drawing at low speed 
Firstly, a study at laborator y scale of different polymer pairs will be carried out by AIMPLAS using a BRABENDER 
torque rheometer, which is a discontinuous mixer to adjust additive ratios and processing conditions of the 
selected formulations. The rheometer consists of a 55 cm 3 mixing chamber with twin screws . This unit sets the 
temperature of the mixing chamber and the screws speed. During the mixing process, the evolution of the torque 
and processing temperature versus time is recorded, allowing to study the influence of the differen t parameters 
and of the specific formulation on the viscosity and stability of the compound. This procedure will obtain different 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 46 of 70 
formulations of compounds in batches of around 40-50g. 
Polymer pairs which have appropriate rheological and thermal properties  will be evaluated on a 
compounding/drawing line at CTB. The compounding section will be followed by a drawing stage allowing to 
produce thick stretched filaments with a limited speed. This extrusion setup will be used to confirm the formation 
of a microfi brillar phase with each of the selected polymer pairs. To increase the adhesion betwee n the two 
polymers, different compatibilizers will be tested. The extrudates will be characterized by standard analysis 
techniques to evaluate the extrusion process: rheo logy (MFI and capillary rheology), transitions in polymer 
structure (DSC and MDSC) and microscopic structure (microscopy and SEM). A small DOE (design of experiments 
including the influence of extrusion screw speed, extrusion temperature, roller speed, dra wing ratio, type and 
concentration of compatibilizer, etc.) may be needed to optimize the extrusion process in terms of microfibril 
formation, fibril size and shape.  
Once the correct polymer grades, concentration and preliminary extrusion conditions have been selected, CTB will 
produce pellets with microfibrillated morphology by pelletisin g the extrudate from their extrusion line. The 
production of the precompounded micr ofibrillar reinforced formulation will be further upscaled by PLANET to 
supply to WP5. 
Subtask 3.4.2 Further processing of precompounded microfibrillar reinforced formulation 
The materials generated in task 3.4.1 (pelletized compounds with bio-PET and bio-PA microfibrils) will be evaluated 
in terms of their processability in different plastic processing lines: injection moulding, foil extrusion and textile 
fibre extrusion. Care should be taken that the microfibrillar structure produced during the compounding step is 
not destroyed in the new melt process. This implies that the processing tempe rature will be kept considerably 
lower than the melting temperature of the fibrils (PET or PA). The extrusion temperature is in this case moderate 
(ca. 200 -240°C). The presence of the non -molten microfibrillar structures in the polymer melt might cause 
extrusion problems especially at filters and in the die or spin -packs where the polymer h as to pass through fine 
cross sections. It can be required to adjust the die or the spin-packs or to remove the filters to obtain an acceptable 
processability. The amount  of PET or PA in the formulation in this subtask will be limited to maximum 10% to 
minimize this risk. It also needs to be evaluated if drawing of the foil / filament is still possible to the same extent 
as drawing of a homopolymer foil / filament without breaking the microfibrils or disturbing the internal matrix 
structures (creation of vo ids). Following parameters are important in the optimization process: temperature 
profile, shear rate, mass flow, draw ratio etc. The formed injection moulded products, f oils and filaments will be 
fully characterized with a focus on the property improvemen ts thanks to the fibrillar reinforcements (tensile 
strength & modulus, creep, barrier properties, impact resistance, etc.). Films/ sheets will be provided to task 2.5.  
Subtask 3.4.3 In-line formation of the microfibrillar structure 
In the case of foil and filament extrusion, the development of a fibrillar polymer structure would preferentially be 
obtained via a single -step extrusion process, without the need of a prelimin ary compounding step. This process 
will start from a dry blend of both polymers (and a  compatibilising agent) that is dosed in the feeder of the 
extrusion line.  
The same grades of matrix and fibril-forming polymer as used in task 3.4.1 will be selected. Next to the formulation 
with up to 10% fibril-forming polymer, also formulations with a  higher amount will be selected (e.g. 60:40). In 
contrast to task 3.4.2, the temperature of the screw and the die or the spinneret should be high enough to allow 
melting the polyester/polyamide fraction. Consideration will be paid to avoid thermal degradat ion of matrix 
polymer. If needed, extra stabilized grades will be used. CTB and AIMPLAS will produce foils/sheets and textile 
filaments that will be further stretched on the extrusion line in order to induce the fibril formation. Maximizing 
elongation and orientation of the fibrils is crucial. The produced foils and filaments will be again fully characterized 
as in task 3.4.2 and supplied to task 2.5 in order to produce multilayer structures.  
Subtask 3.4.4 Monitoring strategy for microfibrillar structure analysis 
In this task IRIS will develop an optical monitoring system to monitor the formation of the microfibrils within the 
composites as the morphology is a key parameter to the obtained performances. It is envisaged to test first the 
direct imaging possibly with polarization enhancement. In case such vision system cannot reach the required size 
resolution, indirect approaches such as extinction or laser diffraction that could correlate the microfibrils’ 
diameters across the analyzed filament section will be tested and calibrated against off line tests (e.g. TEM/SEM…). 
Tests will be performed in static (off line) configuration on sample materials with different microfibril sizes 
provided by CTB. After an initial design phase for a suitable test rig, the com ponents (light source, beam shaping 
and imaging optics, detector and data acquisition hardware) will be selected from commercially available options 
whenever possible and customized when necessary. The software needed for driving the device, processing the  
data and delivering the results will be designed. The right modelling/ imag e analysis package will be embedded. 
The initial results will allow a quick detection of the morphology “at line” but the techniques will be selected for 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 47 of 70 
their potential to be transferred post project to an inline monitoring configuration.

Objectives  
• To set-up sorting protocols for the different developed materials 
• To develop delamination technologies for PRESERVE multilayer films 
• To set up reprocessing of monomaterials using standard upcycling approaches and applying the principle 
of microfibrillar reinforcement for reprocessing multimaterial biopolymers 
• To develop enzymatic recycling approaches for polyesters and delamination  and to recover polyesters 
monomers/oligomers which will be reused to obtain new copolymers with targeted properties for specific 
applications 
• To examine the biodegradation of the developed coatings, adhesives and compounds in different 
environments in order to define biological EoL options and impact of accidental spill and to demonstrate 
increased biodegradability of PLA with embedded enzymes 
• To investigate the suitability of organic recycling by composting and/or anaerobic digestion 
Description of work  
Task 4.1. Protocols to detect automatically the different PRESERVE materials  
Leader: IRIS - Partners involved: ROMEI and materials providers from WP2, 3 and 5 (IVV, AIMPLAS, CTB, SUDPACK, 
GPI, SIBO…)  
The goal is to prove the ability to sort the novel materials developed in PRESERVE from other conventional 
commodities plastic ending together in the plastic waste stream s, so they can then be handled through their 
respectively adequate organic or mechanical recycling stream (multilayer with different coatings that may trigger 
delamination, MR PC, enzymated blends, e tc.), e .g. in case of mixed recyclable wastes or of inaccurate initial 
organic fraction separation at the consumer level. Samples will be supplied along the fine-tuning of the materials 
in WP2-3 and IRIS will use near infrared spectroscopy (NIR), hyper spectral imaging (HSI in the visible/ short wave 
IR and NIR ranges) and other photonic techniques as required to test the accuracy of the distinction among 
different materials thanks to digital image processing and chemometric analysis of the obtained spectra  initially 
established for each mate rial and system independently. For meeting the requirements of all materials under 
study, the combination of results from different sources is expected to be required. The most suitable approach 
will be discussed with ROMEI and recommended for post project implementation in waste managers or recyclers’ 
sorting line. Once final materials are available from WP5, their correct identification will be verified.  
Task 4.2. Material separation via coating removal 
Leader: PLANET - Partners involved: ROMEI, IRIS, PLATO, CTB, GPI (for all subtasks) 
Subtask 4.2.1 Optimal conditions for material separation 
PLANET will be testing different water-based solutions with salts, and enzymatic detergents at different 
temperatures and pH in or der to establish the most performing conditions such as time, temperature and 
concentration of detergents versus the amount of plastic , which layers have to be separated, in terms of 
efficiency/cost/sustainability. First, PLANET will optimize the treatments in laboratory tests, on hundreds grams of 
the selected plastic multilayers from WP2, alone and in mixture with other plastic waste (e.g. monolayer films), 
allowing the separation of the layers while keeping with best potential for future industry transfe r thanks to 
greater materials availability. ROMEI will shred the plastic waste in their facilities and then provid e it to PLANET. 
The separation of the layers in films including whey -protein barrier coatings was previously achieved by washing

Biodegradation, compostability and materials recycling 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 48 of 70 
out the coatings with tepid water (37 ° C) and/or water at room temperature (20 °C) with enzymatic detergents. 
Alternatively, hot water (50 °C), or water containing specific salts, selected by PLANET could be used. Tests will be 
done with the different types of coatings /primers/adhesives combina tions that shall be removed to find , if 
possible, a versatile process. The different layers will then be tentatively separated by density  or hydrocyclone 
separation, at PLATO facilities, and the different polymeric layers will be characterized in terms of their molecular 
weight, rheological and thermal properties in order to estimate their possible performances in re-processing. CTB 
will support in screening the composition of the materials, and optimization of water bath, in terms  of selection 
of detergents or salts to be added to improve materials separation, applying Hansen Solubility Parameters to 
predict the dissolution capacity of the different adhesives among polymer layers. In the case of coated board and 
pulp packaging, rep ulping trials will be perf ormed at GPI before and after coating removal to devise the best 
approach in terms of compromise between process effectiveness and quality of the recovered fibres . The 
separated PHA will be reformulated as new coating tested in the production of the shampoo bottles in WP5. 
Subtask 4.2.2 Design and production of a pilot for material separation 
Using PLANET’s results from previous subtask, PLATO will design a specific pilot for the delamination and 
multilayers material density separation that will then be placed at ROMEI facilities. The plant will have a capacity 
of up to 10 Kg of plastic materials per batch to be treated, with raw multilayer material at the entry and separated 
monolayer materials at the exit. PLATO will also analyze the liquid water streams at the exit from the plant. ROMEI 
will use the pilot plant in their facilities to treat the PRESERVE materials initially from WP2 and provide them to 
PLANET for testing in laboratory scale for chemical, thermal, and morphological properties.  
Consequently materials, in the order of a few kilos per type,  coming from the pilot trials in WP5 and adequately 
sorted in task 4.1 will be recovered in the pilot to compare the properties with virgin polymers and define which 
treatment for multilayers separation optimally preserve the properties of the polymers for being re-processed for 
the production of new materials  (iteration with task 4.3)  based on known standard for plastic recyclates and 
market requirements. The easy removal of labels glued on packaging via the new adhesives will also be shown at 
PLATO. Scaling up options and process/products potentialities will be assessed by ROMEI with the help of PLATO 
on the basis of the achieved results. 
Task 4.3 Upcycled reprocessing of mono - and multimaterial biopolymers using standard upgrading approaches 
and microfibrillar reinforcement 
Leader: CTB  -Partners involved: SILON, AIMPLAS, PLANET, ASU, ROMEI (for all subtasks) 
In this task, the newly developed packaging materials will be evaluated for their recyclability. Different mechanical 
recycling routes will be investigated. For monomaterials (including those delaminated in the previous task), 
standard upgrading approaches will be used . For the bi - and multi -materials that cannot be separated,  the 
principle of the fibrillar reinforcement will be considered to upcycle the properties of the materials as described 
in WP3 for virgin materials. Mixed plastic waste will be treated in such a w ay that fibrillar structures are formed 
and that the recyclability of these more complex material combinations can be guaranteed. Compounds from this 
task will be provided to WP5 to produce the demonstrators from SRMs. 
Subtask 4.3.1 Reprocessing of monomaterials using standard upgrading approaches 
For the raw monomaterial streams, the materials optionally provided by ROMEI from the previous task will, when 
necessary, be shredded and reprocessed either in injection moulded test bars to evaluate their usabili ty in 
injection moulding applications (CTB) and in extruded foi ls (CTB, AIMPLAS) to evaluate the closed loop recycling 
back into foils to be used in new packaging applications. Besides injection moulding and foil extrusion, fiber 
spinning tests will be per formed by CTB and SILON. Both mono - and multifilament extrusion  trials will be 
performed (open loop recycling). The produced textile fibers will be processed into small textile structures in order 
to evaluate their properties. 
The rheological and the mechanical properties of all materials will be measured and compared with the properties 
of the virgin polymers. Since reprocessing might lead to a decrease in mechanical properties, the addition of 
additives will be tested in order to guarantee the mechanical properties and to obtain properties comparable with 
the properties of the virgin biopolymers. In order to perform a fast screening, PLANET will perform tests with a 
Haake Minijet extruder, working on few grams of material. Different chain extenders such as  Joncryl, nucleating 
agents such as LAK, PDLA, functional molecules such as epoxy plasticizers, functionalized oligomers of lactic acid, 
will be tested. 
Moreover, eBeam treatment as described in WP3 will be applied by ASU to upcycle the recycled biopolymers. The 
study of  eBeam effect will start with standard reprocess ed plastics available at ROMEI and SILON before the 
materials recovered from the project are ready. 
The introduction of high mechanical strengths PLA fibers, specific for PLA matrices will be investigated by CTB to  
create PLA waste matrix self -reinforced structures as described in WP3, aiming to upgrade PLA packaging waste

              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 49 of 70 
into materials with high added value.  
Subtask 4.3.2 Reprocessing of bi-materials 
When reprocessing bi - and multimaterials, typically lower mecha nical properties are obtained due to a poo r 
compatibility of the different polymer types. Co -extruded foils will be initially prepared by CTB: bio -PET and bio-
PE, bio-PA and bio-PE. In a later stage, they will come from WP5 demonstrators. These coextruded materials will 
be recycled as blends, with out separation of the different materials. Recycling as such would lead to inferior 
mechanical properties even after compatibilization. In contrast, p rocessing these polymer blends by applying a 
high drawn ratio and creating a microfibrillar structure will create a remarkably broad spectrum of properties. The 
principle of microfibrillar reinforcement as described in WP3 will be applied on recycled biopolymer blends in 
order to increase significantly the mechanical and barrier properties and to upcycle to biobased waste polymers. 
The different processing routes as described in WP3 will be evaluated: injection moulding after precompounding 
in order to generate a microfibrillar reinforced formulation (CTB), and direct formation of a microfibrillar structure 
using foil extrusion (CTB, AIMPLAS) and textile fiber extrusion (CTB, SILON). Additionally, compatibilisers will be 
added (PLANET) and an eBeam treatment will be applied by ASU as described in WP3 in order to enhance the 
polymer compatibility and the resulting properties. 
Task 4.4. Enzymatic recycling and material upcycling  
Leader: UNIBO  - Partners involved: AIMPLAS 
Initially, the enzyme screening and development of the depolymerization protocol will be carried out on pure PLA. 
Then, prototypes obtained in other WPs will be used to further optimize the protocol. A number of commercially 
available hydrolytic enzymes (esterases, lipases, cutinases, etc.) will be screened to identify those able to degrade 
the selected target bioplastic. To this aim, thin polymer  films will be used and their degradation rate evaluated 
through gravimetric weight loss measurement, while the enzymes preferential cleavage activity  (endo- and/or 
exo-) will be assessed via analysis of monomers release (via HPLC-MS) and oligomers release (via solvent extraction 
and 1H-NMR) in the solution. Those exhibiting the highest degradation rate and a prevalent endo-cleavage activity 
will be selected for the development and optimization of the process for the production and recovery of polyesters 
oligomers. In particular, the average MW of the produced oligomers (via GPC), as well as the amount of monomers 
released (via HPLC -MS) will be evaluated after different reaction times under different pH and temperature 
conditions. In addition, the hydrolysis reaction will be investigated using water/organic solvent biphasic systems. 
Enzyme immobilization/protection st rategies will also be taken into account in order to increase the enzyme 
stability in the biphasic system. Purification protocols of the release d by-products from biodegradation will be 
settled up. The enzymatic degradation process will be upscaled (AIMPLAS) in order to obtain sufficient amount of 
extracts for the further activities. 
Indeed, monomers and/or oligomers so obtained will be characterized and chemically modified in order to obtain 
macromolecular structures that can fit the requests of specific a pplications, adhesives and coatings for textiles, 
that will be developed in WP2. Oligomers at moderate molecular weights with controlled terminal groups will be 
prepared and copolymers with multifunctionalities will be synthesized. The continuous flow of i nformation with 
partners of WP2 and WP5 working in the preparation of prototypes will allow UNIBO to improve the design of 
polymeric structures suitable for the chosen applications. 
Task 4.5. Biodegradability assessment in different environments  
Leader: OWS  -Partners involved: Partners of WP2 and WP3, especially CARB 
The coatings and adhesives developed in WP2 and compounds of WP3 as well as der ived films will be evaluated 
for biodegradation according to international standards in different environments such as for example freshwater 
(ISO 14851), soil (ISO 17556), mari ne (ASTM D6691), compost (ISO 14855) and anaerobic digestate (ISO 15985). 
This will allow to determine possible biological end -of-life options (e.g. composting) and suitable applications of 
developed products, but also will indicate the impact of accidental litter into the environment. One of the 
innovative outcomes of the project is to develop a PLA material with embedded enzymes in order to increase the 
biodegradation rate and moreover establish biodegradation in mild conditions. As biodegradation testing  takes 
time, these developed PLA compounds will be evaluated early in the proje ct to degrade in compost at ambient 
temperature (28°C) and, when positive, in other environments at mild conditions. The maximum allowed test 
duration to obtain complete biodegr adation is 1 year for home composting. The results will be directly 
communicated to partners of WP2 and WP3 in order to perform modifications if needed to ensure sufficient 
biodegradation rates. Selected formulations meeting the respective biodegradation criteria for organic recycling 
or home composting where applicable will be recommended for scaling up of the demonstrator solutions in WP5. 
Task 4.6. Organic recycling and home composting  
Leader: OWS  -Partners involved: Partners of WP5 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 50 of 70 
Selected packaging demonstrators from WP5 will be evaluated for suitability for organic recycling by industrial 
composting in line with EN 13432 Requirements for packaging recoverable through composting and 
biodegradation - Test scheme and evaluation criteria for the final acceptance of packaging (2000) and by home 
composting in line with NF T 51 -800 Plastics – Specifications for plastic suitable for home composting  (2015) (no 
standard on European level is yet available), which is similar to the certification systems OK compost HOME of TÜV 
AUSTRIA Belgium and DIN-Geprüft home compostable. This does not only involve biodegradation testing, but also 
material characteristics (mainly heavy metals), disintegration and effect on plant toxicity. Disintegration, which is 
the physically falling apart of a material, is strongly influenced by thickness and density and will be carefully 
examined and therefore the partners will be requested to provide a range of samples with variable attributes. 
Results will be communicated to WP5 partners. Furthermore, the new concept of organic recycling by treatment 
in industrial b iogasification plants will be evaluated. Therefore, not only the biodegradation, but also the 
disintegration under anaerobic conditions will be evaluated with the option of subsequent aerobic composting to 
represent industrial biogasification plants with additional composting step.  
Deliverables  
D4.1 EoL material monitoring (M36)- Report on the capacity to automatically sort the new materials for the correct 
waste management and recommendation for future use in sorting facilities, linked to task 4.1  
D4.2 Enzymatic recycling (M36)- Report on enzymatic degradation; linked to tasks 4.4 
D4.3 Biodegradation of developed materials in different environments under home composting and anaerobic 
conditions (M36)- Interim report on biodegradation behavior linked to task 4.5  
D4.4 Material separation (M36)- Report on pilot plant for materials separation and resulting recovered materials, 
linked to task 4.2  
D4.5 Recycling of biomaterials (M42)- Final report on the upcycling routes for recycled biobased packaging waste 
from WP5 including upgraded reprocessing,  microfibrillar-reinforcement and final enzymatic re cycling routes as 
well as eBeam effect to upcycle SRM but also resulting upcycled SRM samples for WP5, linked to task 4.3 and 4.4  
D4.6 Biodegradation, organic recycling of packaging by industrial and anaerobic digestion and home composting 
(M48)- Final report on biodegradation behavior, organic recycling and home composting linked to tasks 4.6 
 
 
Objectives  
The WP focuses on processing WP2, 3 and 4 (SRM) materials to convert into final packaging with bio-content >85% 
at pilot scale. The reprocessed materials will also be tested for processing into textiles and composites with less 
than 15% of added virgin materials. The main objectives of this WP are: 
• To develop novel eco-design concepts for the production of the multilayer structures for packaging, and 
for textile/composites applications, with the focus on sustainability and recyclability 
• To appropriately combine the previously developed upcycling approaches and to produce single and 
multilayer packaging materials for final prototype packaging with upcycled bio-based materials  
• To evaluate their functional performance, compare it to those of the packaging materials produced using 
the fossil-based counterparts and to validate the suitability of the upcycled materials for food packaging 
• To produce textiles and composites from secondary raw materials coming from WP4 and to validate the 
quality of the upcycled materials for non-food packaging applications. 
Description of work  
Task 5.1. Novel Eco-design approaches for improved recycling and biodegradation of plastics for packaging, textiles 
and composites 
Leader: IVV   Partners involved: AIMPLAS, IVV, SUDPACK, ASU, CTB, SIBO, MDLZ, GPI, DANONE, DENIMX  
Novel eco-design approaches will be provided for the packaging and textiles in close collaboration with task 2.5 
activities. Eco-design means a useful combin ation of different materials to maintain desired techno -functional 
properties (e.g. barrier to assure shelf -life of  packed food), but also preferred end -of-life route such as 
biodegradation or material recycling. Initially planned packaging (food and cosme tics), textiles and composites 
that are to be taken into consideration for the final demonstrators are shown in the table below. The structures 
for the packaging will be revisited under the lead of IVV based on WP1 requirements and WP2/3/4 results as well 
as taking into account the preliminary LCA/LCC results from WP6. The results of the WP4 as well as the DSS will be

Task 5.2. Upscaling of food packaging production and functional characterisation 
Leader: SUDPACK   Partners involved: DANONE, MDLZ, IVV, CTB, PLANET, ROMEI, PLATO, OWS, DENIMX 
The structures defined in Task 5.1 will be produced for testing the upscalability  in packaging of the upcycled 
compounds and coatings from WP3 and 2 respectively. Flexible food packaging production at TRL 5 will initially be 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.

Page 52 of 70 
performed by IVV and AIMPLAS. IVV will perform the coating of protein/PHA, metallization on bio -plastics (bio-
PET, PLA) and on protein coatings and bio-adhesive lamination processes. Optionally, FA grafting will be applied 
as indicated in Table 5.1. AIMPLAS will perform the compounding, extrusion of films and, coatings on cardboard. 
The coating and lamination processes of selected structures will be upscaled to TRL 6 at SUDPACK for flexible bio-
based food packaging on an inline roll -to-roll coating line and GPI for the board -based laminates. SUDPACK will 
process the PLA as a sealing f ilm using blown -film extrusion, providing a smooth surface for sealing and also 
optional metallization (performed by IVV) for the high -barrier lidding film of the dairy product (P hiladelphia 
Cheese, product of MDLZ).  IVV and SUDPACK will also coextrude bio PE/bioPA films subsequently at TRL 5 and 6 
respectively. They will also thermoform the trays where applicable. GPI will upscale the fibre-based cups/trays at 
TRL 6 and DANONE will obtain from their related business partner pulp moulded bottles , which will be coated 
using optimized PHA formulations coming from WP2. ASU/NTT will treat some of the obtained packaging by eBeam 
(see Table in Task 5.1)  and they will be compared to untreat ed counterparts. When applicable, labels will be 
applied on packaging using patented biobased adhesives from BOSTIK. 
The upscaled packaging materials will be characterized in terms of their gas (DIN 53380) and water vapour (EN ISO 
15106-3) barrier, and mechanical performance (e.g. adhesion, laminate bond, sealing seam strength after testing). 
The packaging will be provided to next task for validation but also to WP4 for performing the respective organic 
and/or materials recycling approaches  (which efficiency will be evaluat ed by ROMEI, PLATO, OWS, etc.) and to 
WP7 for consumer acceptance tests.  
Task 5.3. Validation of novel food and drinks packaging using upcycled materials  
Leader: MDLZ   Partners involved: DANONE, SUDPACK, IRIS, AIMPLAS 
Trays and films produced in Task 5.2 will be used to pack the different food products. Carton beverage bricks and 
cups/small bottles will be used for the drinks. In each case, a benchmark representing the currently used packaging 
material will be used for comparison. The following food and drink packaging applications are targeted in this Task:  
- Snack pack for nut-chocolate bar, instant cocoa powder by MDLZ  
- Tray and lid for dairy products (Philadelphia cheese) by MDLZ, PA/PE films for MAP or vacuum-packed meat 
- Flexible pouch for dairy products (liquid yoghurt) by DANONE 
- Paper pulp moulded small bottles for dairy products (yoghurt and milk) by DANONE 
- Cardboard-based beverage bricks for juice drink pack by DANONE 
In terms of packaging validation, IRIS will perform the initial trials (and support the subsequent test campaigns 
especially in case of DANONE or the ESG members) and once the solutions are improved as needed/ pre-selected, 
the final series of tests of the final packaging prototypes will be handled by the industrial end users. The shelf life 
will be tested (via physical-chemical, microbiological and organoleptic studies). At several storage periods, analyses 
of different parameters (appearance, colour, odour, pH, moisture content, lipid-oxidation, etc.) will be carried out. 
Easy emptying effect of FA-grafting will be tested for cheese and possibly other products if needed. Depending on 
WP2 results, also antimicrobial properties of the grafted PHA coatings will be tested. DANONE and MDLZ will then 
validate the final packaging on the tested food to follow the product shelf life. The performance assessments will 
be performed with the packages using various products; such as water, fatty, acidic and neutral products, in 
storage conditions at least for about two months. Recommendations for further improvements in task 5.2 in case 
shelf life is not reaching the targets will be provided in terms of the process, structure/formulation. 
Recommendations will be given in terms of the suitability of the developed solutions for packagin g different 
products including those from ESG members such as CocaCola (e.g. PRESERVE drink containers and bottles) and 
Manor (in terms of validating the PA/PE films for packing chicken based products ) and application notes 
summarising the main findings will be prepared for the relevant associations in the ESG.  
Task 5.4 Processing and Validation of SRM into textiles, composites and packaging for personal care 
Leader: SILON -Partners involved: CTB, ITENE, BDF, DENIMX 
The SRM resulting from the recycling of the food packaging from the previous tasks will be provided by WP4 where 
the r-bio PE and r-PLA will be upcycled by CTB, r-bio PET and r-bio PE will be compounded by PLANET and ROMEI 
(TRL 6) from delaminated materials and, from the latter, cast films will be produced by SUDPACK.  
The following textile and composite applications are targeted in this task for validation.  
- Packaging produced by SIBO for cosmetics and personal care products (BDF) 
- Packaging textiles (non-woven bags) (SILON, CTB) 
- Composites (Carrier boxes and cases) (DENIMX) 
The flexible packaging from SRM for personal care will include r-bio PET and r-bio PE as substrate and sealing film, 
respectively (IVV TRL5, SUDPACK TRL6). The production of rigid cosmetics packaging will initially be performed by 
injection moulding process at AIMPLAS / CTB and will be upscaled finally at SIBO  for personal care injected jars, 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 53 of 70 
and by injection blow moulding for the small bottles in combination with in-mould PHA labelling process. Cosmetic 
jars, bottles and flowpacks will be characterized in terms of oxygen and water vapour permeability and mechanical 
properties (see task 5.2).  
BDF will validate the final packaging on their products (cosmetic jars and bottles - oil in water emulsions; flowpacks 
- wetwipes) following the product shelf life by looking at weight loss of the product, stability to light, perfume loss 
testing, product appearance and functionality (tests can last up to 8 months at different temperatures). 
More complex polymer combinations, which could not  be separated into individual polymers will be processed 
into textile fibres using high drawn processes leading to the formation of microfibrillar structures. First pilot scale 
textile fibre extrusion test will be performed  at CTB  and once its performance is verified, upscaling will be 
performed by SILON in order to produce textile fibers and non-woven materials. The textiles will be coated by CTB 
in order to reduce the release of microplastics as developed in WP2 and manufactured into shopping bags. Fibers 
and final textile products will be tested (strength, creep behavior, appearance, …). Textile proper performance and 
validation of possible microfibre release will be characterized by ITENE (following WP2 approach). 
Recycled PLA materials will be upgraded by self-reinforcement (CTB). Highly-drawn PLA reinforcing fibres and films 
will be combined with a matrix of the same polymer family, making it lighter, more impact resistant and improving 
recycling possibilities. As such, SRPC bio-based composite prototypes based on PLA will be produced by CTB and 
further upscaled and demonstrated by DENIMX into carrier boxes and/or cases. The performance will be compared 
to the performance of the currently used materials such as a standard  PP transport boxes. Analyses of different 
parameters (appearance, colour, odour, impact resistance, mechanical strength, …) will be carried out.

Objectives  
• To address the environmental Life Cycle assessments of the developed materials and final packaging products 
through their value chain and support eco-design principles implementation.  
• To determine the CAPEX a nd OPEX of the different stages associated with  the development of the target 
materials and production of new packaging products.  
• To identify and assess social aspects and overcome any possible related issues.  
• To define indicators that will be assessed f or determining how circular the value chain of the materials and 
products developed within PRESERVE is.  
• To assess health and safety risks aligned with applicable laws and regulations to guide the project 
implementation according to industry best practices. 
Description of work  
Task 6.1 Environmental Life Cycle assessment (LCA) and eco-design  
Leader: NTT - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
In this task, the potential environmental impacts of the new materials and packaging will be performe d. The LCA 
analysis will involve the following stages: definition of scope and goal, development of relevant inventory inputs 
and outputs, assessment of their potential impacts and interpretation of results within the context of proposed 
new materials and products. The LCA will be carried out considering the guidelines of ISO 14040/14044. The 
environmental impact categories that will be analyzed include: global warming potential, human toxicity, 
ecotoxicity, resources use and depletion, energy demand among others. After checking the sensitivity  and 
reliability of the study, relevant conclusions and recommendations will be drawn. The LCA will be performed with

Safety, Environmental and Economic Sustainability assessments
