the specialized software Simapro 8. The participation of technology developers and demonstrator´ leaders will be 
required to provide infor mation for the inventories of LCA Analysis. It is envisaged that the results of this study 
will demonstrate the positive environmental impacts of implementing PRESERVE materials into new packaging 
products, compared with their counterparts on the market, at the demonstrators’ level. Eco-design principles will 
be implemented  in link with task 5.1  based on environmental impacts´ outcomes. Eco -design will enable 
incorporating environmental considerations into the new produ cts design as well as other p rinciples like 
recyclability, potential secondary use. The entire life cycle of the new materials and products will be considered, 
and recommendations for eco-design will be applied early in the product development process (alt hough 
continuous improvement of all processes will be performed  based on i dentified hot spots). As such, an interim 
LCA will be delivered by mid-term to guide the selection of the materials for the final demonstrators.  
 
Task 6.2 Life Cycle Cost and cost-feasibility  
Leader: NTT - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
This assessment will measure and analyze the capital, operational costs and cost variations resulting from applying 
the proposed technologies for each of the stages in the materials life cycle and packaging product’s supply chain. 
This analysis will be done by performing a Life Cycle Cost analysis (LCC). The LCC will present a similar structure 
and will be conducted in parallel to the LCA (in terms of functional unit and approach). The analysis will be 
developed in two basic steps: cost identification and a cost benefits analysis. Therefore, as soon as the process 
chain for the manufacturing of the new materials and their corresponding packaging are established, cost models 
can be set up to estimate the product costs as a function of various parameters including volume of the batches, 
processes used, type of materials, supplies and other inputs etc. This model will also guide the process 
optimization e.g. by identifying possible bottl enecks in the process chain. Specific experiments will be designed 
and conducted to obtain parameters for the model or to compare different technologies for a particular step. The 
results of this analysis will make it possible to compare the proposed new materials and products with alternative 
ones, from an economical point of view, and to determine the overall reduction of costs that could be achieved 
using this model in the packaging products value chains. Based on obtained CAPEX and OPEX that will be simulated 
at scales up to 50 times that of the project (as a typical throughput in commercial mechanical recycling plants, 
process for the primary and secondary material), we will conclude in which conditions and for processing which 
materials the proposed production lines are economically feasible to reach to the market. 
 
Task 6.3 Social LCA assessments  
Leader: NTT - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
In this task, the social and socio-economic benefits of implementing the proposed new packaging products will be 
addressed. To this end, the Social LCA (S -LCA) methodology will be applied. The S -LCA is an innovative 
methodology that integrates traditional LCA methodological steps while having social impacts as focus, namely: 
(1) defining goal and scope of the assessment; (2) inventory of the drivers which may lead to an impact; a life cycle 
inventory is elaborated for indicators (e.g. number of jobs created) linked to impact categories (e.g. local 
employment) which are related to five main stakehol der groups (e.g., [i ] worker, [ii] consumer, [iii] local 
community, [iv] society and [v] value chain actors); (3) impact assessment based in the selection and calculation 
of proper indicators of impacts; and (4) interpretation of the results. The S-LCA methodology proposed embeds a 
detailed inventory method tailored on real data, collected directly from the field of application thanks to 
customized surveys that allow modelling the life cycle of the proposed technologies. S -LCA makes use of generic 
and site-specific data, can be quantitative, semi-quantitative or qualitative, and complements the environmental 
LCA and LCC. Categories such as health and safety; jobs creation; working conditions; well-being among others will 
be addressed. The envisaged positive results will constitute valuable inputs to stimulate preferences for these new 
materials and packaging technologies and will also be used as part of the baseline information aimed to design an 
adequate strategy to increase job opportunities, stakeholders and consumer’s acceptance. 
 
Task 6.4 Circularity assessment and DSS  
Subtask 6.4.1 Scoping of the data and scenarios - Leader: ITENE – Partners involved: NTT, IRIS 
In a first stage, identification of opportunities for circular value capture will be addressed. This activity will include 
the searching of technical, economic, social and environmental opportunities that allows promoting a circularity 
approach of PRESERVE’s materials and related packaging products. In a second stage, a circular KPIs assessment 
will be realized, as a  first step, appropriate circular economy indicators will be defined for PRESERVE technology 
through the complete value chain to assess how circular the PRESERVE’s materials flows are. The analysis will start 
at raw materials procurement stage and finalize at the end of life scenarios. Feedback from the technical WPs will 
be needed to establish the required KPIs, such as the amounts of raw materials, the masses of unrecoverable 
waste and the utility factor indicator. As a second step, co mplementary indicators that will allow addressing 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 55 of 70 
additional impacts and risks will be considered. Those include material price variation, supply chain risks, scarcity 
among others. As a third step, the transition towards a circular economy in the new mate rials development and 
packaging products production value chain will be measured and evaluated. Finally, in a third stage, different 
circularity scenarios will be evaluated. Potential scenarios will be analysed in -depth to improve the PRESERVE 
circularity. The four ways of circular value creation will be addressed: (1) the power of short cycle, (2) the power 
of long cycle, (3) the power of cascades and (4) the power of pure circles. This last stage will receive feedback from 
task 6.1 related to eco -design outcomes and from WP 4 and WP5. Policymakers’ recommendations including 
design for circularity, use of primary and secondary materials, recycling/ upcycling routes will be provided. 
Subtask 6.4.2 Sustainability enhancement decision support system (DSS) -Leader IRIS, Partners involved: NTT, 
ITENE, DENIMX 
This task will combine the information gained from 6.1 and 6.2 and scenarios developed in the previous subtask 
to support the decisio ns of the different stakeholders involved along the value chain towards sus tainability 
optimization and the best upcycling approach thanks to the development of a user-friendly automatic tool (app). 
Using advanced artificial intelligence techniques, IRIS w ill design a  multiparametric DSS to help in the materials 
and EoL/secondary application selection. Based on data at different levels of the value chain, it will simulate 
different linear and circular pathways and allow identifying the best routes along the life cycle of the new materials 
taking into account the confidence factors for each scenario, the perspectives of the different stakeholders, as 
well as their priorities for optimisation. The DSS derived app will allow to provide tailored information to t he 
PRESERVE product development to reduce environmental burden and increase  resource efficiency among the 
tested cases. In particular, the alpha version of the app will be tested by DENIMX to support the final ecodesign of 
the demonstrators from SRM in WP5  which results will be taken into account to obtain the final version. 
Conclusions and recommendations to decision -makers (e.g. materials formulators and products designers, 
recyclers and end users’) will be provided as readily understandable, complete and consistent presentation of the 
impacts and sustainability.  
 
Task 6.5 Identification and assessment of regulatory requirements  
Subtask 6.5.1. Evaluation of the legal framework regarding the risk assessment of the prototypes packaging (Safe 
by Design concept integration) - Leader: ITENE – Partners involved: all to provide required inputs  
The aim of the European Food Law is to ensure a high level of protection of human life and consumers’ interests 
regarding food. So that, there is a need to assess the compliance with applicable regulations to food contact 
materials. In order to achieve this objective, the safe -by-design methodology will be applied and implemented 
throughout the project, which will enable the integration of anticipated safety impacts of any material or additive 
into the design or production phases of the prototypes. This task will consist of  three stages:  (i) developing and 
improving methodologies for materials design considering toxicity and other life cycle aspects, (ii) using thematic 
research, development and innovation to overcome challenges where safer alternatives have been difficult to find, 
and (iii) creating an environment that enables the concept through knowledge exchange, education, and supply 
chain cooperation.  
Additionally, legislation applicable to the developments resulting from the project will be identified, to ensure the 
compliance with food contact materials legislation. In order to release the new development at commercial scale, 
legal requirements need to be fulfilled and evaluated over a final product produced at industrial scale. Considering 
this, it might be required to proceed with specific documentation to ensure the food contact safety of developed 
materials. Therefore, it is considered to carry out some work in advance in this task with the materials developed 
within the project to characterise its behaviour, providing a preliminary evaluation. This evaluation will be finished 
by each one of the developers or owners before arriving to commercial scale, falling out of the scope and work of 
the project. This task will particularly support the collection of trials linked to the food contact approval of 
enzymated compounds from task 3.1. This task will be carried out based on results from WP1 and 2.  
Subtask 6.5.2. Compliance of the prototypes with EU Food Contact Materials regulations Leader: ITENE  
Migration analyses of the prototypes will be conducted to verify compliance with food contact materials 
regulations. In this sense, overall migration, specific migration of additives, metals and primary aromatic amines, 
as well as NIAS evaluation (non-intentionally added substances) will be studied during the assessment. These 
analyses will be carried out by ITENE according to the information and materials provided by the partners 
developing the prototype packaging.

Objectives  
The overall objectives are:   
• To study consumer perception and acceptance of the newly developed (upcycled) bio-based packaging  
• To document undertaken and proposed dissemination and communication activities.  
• To ensure clustering and coordination with other related EU/National projects. 
• To ensure the project results reach all the relevant stakeholders who will use and implement them and to 
attract business partners to maximise their exploitation potential.  
• To ensure that the findings from the project are widely communicated to the scientific community and the 
general public and promote policy recommendations 
• To guarantee IPR management according to European Commission Guidelines and Consortium Agreement 
• To establish initial circular value chains to pave the way to the future deployment of the PRESERVE solutions. 
Description of work  
Task 7.1: Study of consumer perception  
Leader ASU - Partners involved: EUBP, KNEIA, NTT, DANONE, MDLZ, BDF, External Stakeholders Group (ESG) 
Consumers will be targeted to anal yse their perception and to assess their confidence in PRESERVE innovative 
solutions. This will ensure the sustained alignment of PRESERVE to real market needs to help decreasing time-to-
market of the proposed soluti ons, i.e. the developed demonstrators. A parallel goal will be to verify that the 
consumer requirements defined in WP1 are perceived accordingly. For this purpose, expert interviews, literature 
research, brand owner surveys will be applied as multipliers to extrapolate consumers’ perception and consumer 
acceptance tests will be performed with the developed PRESERVE demonstrators . This will complement the 
societal assessment (s-LCA) performed in WP6 by NTT. The analysis of the results will consider the gender of the 
respondents to profile the differences in the perception and acceptance of bio-packaging by females vs. males. 
Task 7.2: Standardisation, Policy & Regulatory framework 
Leader EUBP - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
The aim of this task is to evaluate the current EU poli cies and regulations related to bio -based packaging, their 
recycling and upcycling, and the sustainability of bio-packaging products throughout their life cycle with a view to 
proposing the incorporation/modification of these policies to ensure that they take into account environmental, 
social and economic considerations in link with the outcomes of WP6. Relevant standardisation and certification 
landscape for PRESERVE will be continually assessed at international, EU and national level. PRESERVE findings will 
be captured by EUBP for fueling the evolution of different standard s (e.g. regarding recycling, biodegradation, 
recycled and/or bio-based content, etc .), certification (e.g. sustainable sourcing fo r bio -based materials) and 
labelling schemes. An in -depth exchange will be established with the relevant standardisation bodies, technical 
committees (CEN/TC 411 - Bio-based products and CEN/TC 249 - Plastics), and with the most important 
independent certifiers in the field of bioplastics (Vinçotte and DIN CERTCO). EUBP will curate the provision of policy 
recommendations regarding resource efficiency improvement, waste management, recycling and EoL scenarios 
tuned for specific applications, that could be used by standardization bodies in the reflection about new/ improved 
standards. In terms of safety, in link age with WP6, our safe by design approach will consider food contact 
legislation from the project outset and we will also perform migration tests on the  primary as well as secondary 
materials from the project. Incentives such as the fast track approval of the dossier of new food contact bio and / 
or recycled materials with demonstrated reduced environmental impacts will also be assessed as well as proposals 
for related financial support . The outcome of the ev aluation of the project results, especially in terms of

Task 7.3 Communication Activities  
Subtask 7.3.1. Communication Plan and reporting on communication activities - Leader KNEIA - all partners to 
provide required inputs  
As discussed in Section 2.2, we will draw up a Communication Plan that will be effective in engaging with our 
targeted stakeholders during the project, to mobilise their interests and secure their buy -in and support for the 
project. This plan will be close ly linked with the project dissemination activities and it will follow the steps of a) 
identifying all possible stakeholders (CHX, in link with task 7.5); b) organise the stakeholders into “communities of 
support” for helping us to present our ambition, go als, objectives and impacts (CHX); c) Development of the  
PRESERVE brand as a powerful marketing and communications tool (KNEIA); and, d) design and implementing an 
effective communication campaign (KNEIA, EUBP and CHX). An exhaustive mapping of stakeholders will be carried 
out in the initial phase of the project to help design the social media activities, expand the Circular Plastics Helix 
and plan timely clustering ev ents. The analysis will be led by CHX but all partners will strongly contribute by 
reaching their existing stakeholder networks.  In addition to planning and designing our Communication campaign, 
communication reports at project interim and at the end of t he action (D7.2) will document the communication 
activities that have been implemented, an d all associated communication materials will be annexed. An update 
on the results of the project will be provided to the relevant multipliers in order to diffuse the project results 
through both newsletter and presentations within relevant events (e.g. General meetings, Workshops). 
Subtask 7.3.2 Project website - Leader KNEIA - all partners to provide required inputs 
The project website (D7.1) architecture will be car efully planned to effectively cater for the different target 
audiences who, from the central landing page, will be able to navigate easily to dedicated sub-sites depending on 
their particular area of interest. The website will serve as a powerful communica tion tool to all our target 
audiences (it will also house a restricted access area for par tners to store information and facilitate file sharing 
and internal communication). The public site will present the project brand and will contain well-presented non-
confidential project information: project concept, its partners, its core objectives, rel ated literature, easy to 
understand infographics presenting the strategic, competitive and economic benefits of the project, information 
about Horizon 2020, the ‘PRESERVE Green Channel’ of open access publications, links to other relevant websites, 
networks, projects, communities, conferences, etc. The platform will also serve as a tool to disseminate the non-
confidential results of the project (public reports and deliverables, publications as part of our green open access, 
etc.). It will incorporate videos  (official project video and subsequent videos produced by other partners to 
describe parts of the process). At the project end, the relevant public information and results will be available from 
the website, which will be maintained as a central virtual hub for our post-project activities well into the future.  
Subtask 7.3.3 Communication and promotional materials- Leader KNEIA - all partners to provide required inputs 
Project leaflets, posters, project video, newsletters and promotional materials (gadgets for tradeshows, etc.) will 
be designed in order to support project communication and branding efforts. These materials will be reported and 
Annexed to the Communication Reports (D7.2).  
Subtask 7.3.4 Social / digital media channels -Leader EUBP - - Leader KNEIA - all partners to provide required inputs  
This subtask will capitalise on the tremendous potential of reaching some of our targeted audiences through social 
media channels. Informed by the stakeholder analysis, a social media grid will be drawn up to identify the most 
appropriate social media channel/sites for specific audiences. Appropriate pages will be designed for each channel 
and a content maintenance plan will be put in place for managing the streams of information across these channels 
to sec ure and maintain followers. Social and digital med ia will be particularly powerful in helping to create 
‘communities of support’ for the project. Community creation will be achieved via tools such as: Google Meet, 
Reddit, Pinterest and other social media networks such as Facebook, Twitter, LinkedIn and YouTube. The project 
will create interest on social media and digital platforms by using visual media, videos, animations, icons and info-
graphic imagery, and importantly, mobile enabled content and richer content experiences for users of any of the 
digital platforms. EUBP will work closely with CHX to make sure that the appropriate resources are relayed into 
the Circular Plastics Helix.

Task 7.5 Multi-Stakeholders Platform and the Circular Plastics Helix  
Leader CHX - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
This task will be directed towards community building and stakeholder engagement through the Circular Plastics 
Helix, a virtual community of experts in plastic packaging, circularity and recycling. In the frame of PRESERVE, 
Crowdhelix will expand the already existing community and onboard further 100 organisations working in the area 
of bioplastics into the Circul ar Plastics Helix. The Helix will ensure the engagement, inclusion and active 
participation of all relevant stakeholders  (research centres, universities, corporat es, SMEs, networks and 
associations) and their diverse perspectives. The platform can also act as an instrument for knowledge sharing and 
engagement with other successful projects under the Horizon 2020 call CE-BIOTEC-09-2020, and other H2020 and 
future Horizon Europe projects. One of t he roles of th e platform will be to collect the information pro vided by 
industry stakeholders identified during the project in order to define common development campaigns aimed to 
unlock the potentials of PRESERVE strategies in different EU Countries. The Helix will be nourished through reports, 
publications, press briefings and newsletters on project results and other relevant information. In particular, the 
Circular Plastics Helix  will help to define a set of relevant topic s influencing the take -off of biopackaging 
technologies and solutions. Among them, a special focus will be dedicated to: standardization issues, supply chain 
facilitating measures, sustainability criteria development for PRESERVE products. The involvement of stakeholders 
and the valuable inter-communication management strategy will be a crucial aspect to be carried out by all project 
partners. The active collaboration of PRESERVE identified actors will be the basis to achieve the final target.  
Task 7.6: PRESERVE Clustering  
Leader CHX - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
This task will ensure that PRESERVE is networked with all relevant national and international projects, initiatives 
and networks in the EU  and internationally . The primary goals of the clustering activities will be to identify 
synergies in projects’ implementation, work on policy recommendations together, and identify areas for potential 
future projects and exploitation across the actors.  Importantly, and in line with the call text, we will ensure a close 
interaction with the other proposals selected for funding under  the same (CE-BIOTEC-09-2020) or related topics 
(see table 1.4) . This task will foresee the implementation of common dissemination activities among others 
including workshops, conferences and exchange of the newsletters from the other connected projects. T he 
networking plan will take into account relevant projects within international stakeholders and other EU / national 
projects (some of which are identified in Section 1.3). It will also focus on networking between consortium partners 
and their respective areas. Most of the project partners are members of relevant networks, groups , associations 
and initiatives such as the Plastics Circularity Multip lier, Circular Plastics Alliance, Bio -based Industries Joint 
Undertaking (BBI -JU), the SPIRE PPP, SUSCHEM, CEF IC, Plastics Europe, etc. These memberships will be

Task 7.7. Innovation and IPR Management  
Leader KNEIA - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs (all subtasks) 
Subtask 7.7.1. Innovation Notification System Register  
The objective of the Innovation Management process will be the implementation of a systematic approach for the 
mapping, evaluation and definition of the protection strategy options for the key exploitable results KERs, based 
on an expected impact orientation approach. The mapping includes the monitoring of the evolution of the results 
towards market readiness via the review of the TRL evolution of each KER, as well as that of the completion of the 
impact KPIs defined in table 2.1 , while the evaluation implies a) the identification of innovation enablers/driving 
factors and b) determining the link between technical results and market demand, being the main outcome the 
identification of business opportun ities, the related customer segments and which v alue propositions they 
require/need, that will be further developed in the business plan of task 7.8.  
It will be based on an internal Innovation Notification System Register (INSR), as the tool for capturing  and 
managing the research results. On the INSR, each result identified as potentially exploitable will be assessed with 
the support of the Innovation Committee, and will implement also procedures of risk management based on the 
activities described on Tas k 8.2. The IPR  and Exploitation Manager will mak e recommendations concerning the 
need of protection of each output and possible routes. The identification of the results to be protected will be 
discussed briefly in the meetings of the Project Steering Comm ittee in order to assure that no activity to be 
performed might interfere with the protection strategy. 
Subtask 7.7.2. IPR management   
The IPR management strategy for each KER identified in the previous subtask will be defined, and rules will be 
formalized for the use of foreground and required background and its distribution within the project as well as the 
rules for handling sensitive or confidential information. This IPR strategy will be specially focused on the protection 
of the innovations and knowle dge developed within the project, to help on max imizing the returns on the 
investments. On the basis of the outputs of subtask 7.7.1, the main activities to be developed on this subtask are: 
• Identification of ownership of the results, whether individual or joint: Proposals for the division of share of such 
results and base conditions for their exploitation will be proposed by the IPR  and Exploitation Manager. The 
proposals will be made in line with the conditions set out in the CA.  
• Patent search : systematic patents search and analysis will be performed  throughout the project in order to 
ensure the monitoring of technology developments potentially relevant in terms of freedom to operate  and 
results patentability. This search will also allow the detection of overlaps and new potential partners and 
collaborators in terms of implementation of the business plans.  
• IP Protection strategy: for each KER, and considering the business plans developed on task 7.8, the protection 
strategy will be outlined in order to determine the best options to get the full market potential. Each partner will 
be responsible to apply the knowledge protection measures proposed  (as such patent agent fees have been 
budgeted by many partners, see section 3.4). 
Task 7.8 Exploitation of results and Business model development  
Leader KNEIA - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs 
For each of the KERs, a business plan will be drawn up. A draft of these Business Plans, as part of the PEDR, will be 
delivered at M24 (D7.5) and final Plans in M48 (D7.8). Built on the information already provided in Section 2.2, the 
Business Plans will be structured as follows:  
• Planned key exploitable results and their expected key applications: development status, facts and figures that 
facilitate the assessment of the potential impact, differences from existing competing products/services, main 
IPR issues in link with previous task;  
• Exploitation team: partners involved in the exploitation activities providing information on their previous 
experience and business interests, complementing external resources if not in the consortium;

• Market Potential: the potential geographical and economic size of the market, market trends, main competitors

Task 7.9: Roadmap towards 2030  
Leader EUBP - Partners involved: all to provide required inputs  
In line with our exploitation strategy, and based on the assumptions in tables 1.4 and 2.5, we expect our PRESERVE 
solutions to be have shown the potential to substitute more than 60% of the packaging materials by 2030. As such, 
based on the roadmaps of the individual KERs defined in the previous task, a detailed strategy outlining the steps 
to move the PRESERVE solutions from TRL6+ to TRL 9 will be prepared capturing the key findings and remaining 
knowledge gaps arising from the project as well as the interdependences across the supply and value chain. The 
draft version will be discussed in a project-wide event organized by CHX around M36 to get stakeholders feedback 
(task 7.4). This document will end with a set of recommendations contributing to a viable European roadmap for 
the PRESERVE project results uptake and in general for food and drink packa ging upcycling and production from 
renewable sources. Possible transfer of technology to other sectors will also be considered.

Task 8.2: Implementation of the management procedures 
Leader: IRIS. Partner(s) involved: All 
ISO 9001:2008 certified processes and UNE-EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems for R&D&I certified procedures 
are implemented by IRIS in the management of all their projects and  they form part of their continuous quality 
improvement processes. The project man agement procedures that will be followed are: Technical Work Plan 
Review and Update Procedure; Issues Management Procedure; Scope Management Procedure; Risk Management 
Procedure; Conflict Management Procedure; Communication Management Procedure; Document M anagement 
procedure; Quality Management procedure. The necessary templates and documentation for implementing these 
procedures are available in IRIS and will be shared with the partners in a Project Management Handbook at project 
launch. The Project Coordi nator will ensure that all partners are fully briefed on each procedure, how it works, 
and their role in its implementation.  
Different critical project management procedures will be managed in dedicated aspects: 
Risk Management- Risk Management procedures will be in place, whereby the status of the Critical Risks identified 
in Table 3.2b will be continually reviewed, and additional risks and mitigation strategies will be devi sed as 
appropriate. Contingency plans will be brought into play in an early and ti mely fashion, in consultation with the 
Project Steering Committee.  
Data management – According to the data management plan set up in Section 2.2, which will be further refin ed 
in the project management handbook, all data, both for internal curation (e.g. list of samples, nomenclatures, 
standards followed and testing equipment used, trials data, data for LCA, LCC, sLCA and modelling activities in 
WP6 that will be gathered in a  dedicated data basis, etc.) will be hosted in the project intranet and those 
benefitting from Open Access (publications, selected LCA and validation results among others, but also process 
data under a license) for public distributions will be available fr om the project website as well as in OpenAire or 
Cordis among others respectively in case of publications and deliverables. GDPR best practices will be followed 
whenever personal data are involved. The data management will be led by IRIS with support from WP7 leader in 
terms of data relevant to IPR & open access data. 
Responsible research and innovation (RRI) management including ethical aspects involving the following tasks:  
i) Overseeing ethical and societal issues related to the research activities cond ucted within the project (that will 
include the proper handling of data from consumer perception studies- see section 5.1- and the fulfilment of any 
ethical requirements raised during grant preparation);  
ii) Checking the proper implementation of the regulatory aspects pertaining to the validation in WP5-6 and liaising 
with WP7 in terms of checking the proper outreach to policy makers, public and training;  
iii) Overseeing the promotion of gender equality in the project.  
In addition, the proper implementation of the Innovation & Knowledge Management activities will be checked: in 
linkage with WP7, the Coordinator will assist the IPR & Data manager, review progress and proceedings with regard 
to IPR protection, sharing... 
Task 8.3: Coordination with and Reporting to the EC 
Leader: IRIS. Partner(s) involved: All will assist in reporting  
The Coordinator is the sole point of contact between the EC and the project consortium. The Coordinator will 
ensure that all milestones are met and that all reports are prepar ed and delivered to the EC in accordance with 
contractual requirements. IRIS will execute this task that will be greatly facilitated by the internal management 
plan and reporting from the previous tasks.

3.2 Management structure, milestones and procedures 
Organisational structure and decision-making  
The project will be managed by the experienced Project Coordin ator (PC), IRIS. IRIS follows proven project 
management procedures, which adhere to ISO 9001:2008 certified processes and UNE-EN-ISO 166002: Management 
Systems for R&D&I. The organisational structure (Fig. 3.1) consists of the Project Coordinator (the interface with the 
EC), who is supported by a Project Steering Committee in the strategic management of the project. At executive 
management level, the PC is supported in the implementation of the w ork by a Scientific & Technical Committee 
(S&TC) on the one hand and an Innovation Committee (IC) on the other, the roles and decision -making capacity of 
which are discussed below. This is a balanced structure that distributes governance between various pa rtners 
according to their background to allow a good balance in decision and management of different aspects. An External 
Stakeholders Group (ESG) is also included, which consists of a voluntary group of industry actors and stakeholders 
who will engage wit h the project at different points along the work plan.  This bo dy has no voting rights and a 
Confidentiality Agreement will be in place with all ESG members.

Project coordinator  
The Project Coordinator ( Dr. Elodie 
Bugnicourt from IRIS ) is responsible for 
the day to day running of the project, and 
for ensuring that t he work programme 
adheres to its schedule, fulfils its 
objectives, and that the project meets 
the needs and expectations of all t he 
partners. She will be active in steering the 
evolution of the project by closely 
monitoring the work performed by each 
partner. She is responsible for ensuring 
that the project management procedures 
are correctly implemented and that all 
deadlines and o bligations are met. She 
will also act as the communication and 
administrative interface with the EC, to 
carry out the reporting and overall administrative management of the project. Appropriately, she will also in many 
instances act as the public face for the project e.g. in networking events between EU projects or when the project 
receives enquiries by external actors such as press or policy makers. As this is also a leadership role, it requires a 
profile that is sufficiently experienced and capacitated  to supervise the execution of the work programme and 
delegation of the technical and innovation implementation, and having strong communication, team-building, 
motivational, collective problem solving and analytical skills.  
As an organisation, IRIS has demo nstrable experience, the available technical and administrative resources (with a  
long-established and well qualified Project Management Office that will provide support to the Project Manager in 
administrative, financial and contractual management tasks),  linguistic and communications skills to successfully 
perform project management coordination tasks. In terms of the competence  of Dr. Bugnicourt to successfully 
execute this role, she brings a wealth of project management experience from both private cont ract research and 
funded EC projects. In FP7, she leveraged her industry knowledge and expertise to the coordination two “Resea rch 
for SMEs” projects: DURAWOOD (GA nº 232296); and, OPTIJECT (GA nº 262623), as well as an NMP project OliPHA 
(GA nº  280604): Among others, she was also technical manager and heavily involved in the General Steering 
Committee for the “Research for SME As sociations” project, WHEYLAYER ( GA nº 218340-2) and follow up 
Demonstration Activity project WHEYLAYER2 (GA nº 315743). In H2020, she also managed an NMP-Pilots project 
OPTINANOPRO (GA nº 686116) and a SPIRE project called Multicycle (GA nº 820695). Elodie is assertive and capable 
of leading la rge multi -disciplinary and multi -actor teams with proven results. She is very familiar with all the 
modalities and administrative procedures involved in the management of EC research projects, from the grant 
preparation process, preparing and maintaining t he Consortium Agreement, monitoring work, reporting 
requirements, the use of tools for communication with the EC, etc. Prior to this, she has successfully managed R&D 
projects in the chemical industry, and in particul ar in the development of nanocomposites  as well as FRP  and bio-
sourced resins. She has shown herself to be a motivational leader, a fair and intelligent facilitator, with a sound 
understanding not only of materials science but also of process and associated industries. In addition to having been 
involved in some of the projects feeding into Preserve, Elodie is driven by a genuine green awareness, is passionately 
involved in sustainable materials and processes for 10+ years, and she is also the leader of the Innovation Unit in IRIS 
giving her invaluable experience in relation to Innovation Management. 
Project Steering Committee 
To ensure that the project is implemented according to the needs and requirements of all the project partners, and 
to empower each pa rtner organisation with a role in the s trategic management of the project, a Project Steering 
Committee (PSC) is established. It consists of a key representative of each of the beneficiaries. The PSC will meet 
every 6 months - physically or remote ly, where physical meetings are not possible- and extraordinary (remote) 
meetings may be convoked by the Project Coordinator in the event of urgent matters that may arise). PSC Meetings 
will be facilitated through the chair of the Project Coordinator. Through the PSC the partners will closely monitor and 
control the work performed, following the principles of “quality, time, cost”. The Project Milestones (Table 3.2a) will 
be used as a valuable tool for evaluating critical performance and determining whether or not th e project is on 
schedule. In terms of decision making mechanisms , when strategic decisions need to be taken, such as action to 
solve conflicts, action to mitigate critical risks to project implementation, action to manage changes in the work plan, 
decisions in relation to IPR and e xploitation, etc., it will be the responsibility of the Project Coordinator to seek

Scientific & Technical Committee  
The Scientific & Technical Committee (S&TC) is established to take care of scientific and technical (S&T) issues and 
for supporting the Project Coordinator in ensuring th at the S&T objectives and activities of the project are 
successfully accomplished in a  timely manner, taking into account the interdisciplinary approach and the 
interdependence between the technical tasks of the work plan. The S&TC is composed of the WP and task leaders in 
WP1-6 allowing the needed interactions across the WPs developing the key individual technical results.  
The S&TC is chaired by the Scientific &Technical Manager, who will preside over the WP leaders : Prof. Dr. Markus 
Schmid, a Senior Researcher from ASU, whose research specialises in the field of sustainable packaging and who has 
already occupied that role in numerous EU-projects. 
The appointment of the S&TC will greatly facilitate the implementation of his work, especially in view of th e 
ambitious, highly interdisciplinary nature of the activities involved. Whereas the WP leaders, who will themselves be 
fuelled by their task contributors and their teams, will assume responsibility for the implementation of the work 
towards the fulfilment of the associated Project Objectives (and milestones related to the WPs), the S&TC will ensure 
the consistency (selection of processes suitable for later scale up at end users) and compatibility (e.g. amount of 
materials needed for different purposes of v alidation) among WPs within their thematic through the proper 
engagement of the partners and entrusting to the WPs leaders. The Scientific & Technical (S&T) Manager will act as 
facilitator for the integration of the transversal knowledge without losing the  benefit from synergies among the 
different packaging applications and upcycling approaches that can be used both for primary and secondary materials 
thanks to the common partners involved. The S&T Manager will also ensure the seamless integration of the r esults 
by convoking meetings on a regular basis with the implementation teams (virtual ly or on -site meetings will be 
scheduled as appropriate). It is expected that this structure will increase the potential for early identification of inter-
WP scientific or technical risks and WP deviations level that could impact other activities in their thematic to enable 
effective and timely management. Each WP leader will report on the status and progress of the work involved in their 
WP to the Project Coordinator in monthly remote and biannual presential meetings of the S&TC (chaired by the S&T 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 65 of 70 
Manager). While the S&TC will have the mandate to take decisions that relate to the implementation of the workplan, 
any decisions that could affect the scope of the work, its bu dget, or have a strategic impact on the project will be 
escalated via the Project Coordinator to the PSC for voting and decision taking.  
Innovation Committee  
The Innovation Committee (IC) is responsible for identifying and managing innovation from the pr oject. A key goal 
will be to ensure that the project results are effectively protected and exploited to the full for future industrial growth 
and competitiveness. The IC consists of a qualified representative from each beneficiary.  
The I C assumes the impo rtant role of Innovation Management in the project , and as such will manage the 
implementation of the innovation cycle, and the feedback linkages to the development work. It will evaluate the 
knowledge as it is generated in line with its market impacts. It will also ensure that the project results are effectively 
protected and exploited to the full for future industrial growth and competitiveness. Key strategic issues, such as IPR 
protection mechanisms, IPR sharing and routes to exploitation will be discussed extensively during the IC meetings. 
The IC will also ensure that Business and Exploitation Plans are further developed based on the draft in Section 2.2.  
The IC will be chaired by the IPR & Exploitation Manager , Cristina Barragan (KNEIA) who will lead the partners in 
effective management of the innovation cycle of t he project. She will also act as a driver for the industrial partners 
in defining the post-project concerted value chain commercial strategy and for assisting the partners in identifying 
and managing innovation from the project, advising on the scope and potential IPRs arising from the project. She has 
a master in Communication Sciences and more than 15 years of experience in innovation management, which is a 
core mission of KNEIA, company she founded, therefore a perfect background for this role. She will be supported by 
Dr. Christian Schulz (EUBP) who will also act as Communication & Dissemination Manager–his biopolymer/ renewable 
resources management  scientist education, strong track record in leading dissemination and deployment 
programmes in collaborative environments will strengthen his capacity for accurate communication fundamental for 
the role which is very aligned with the main mission of EUBP in the transfer of knowledge to the process industry. He 
will be responsible for leading the consortium in further planning and implementing the project Communication and 
Dissemination activities, as well as ensuring the project reaches out to different audiences in the most effective way, 
and will also ensure the confidentiality of the results is safeguarded until the IP is protected.  
The IC will meet regularly (at least every 6 months) and pay attention to discerning IP at regular checkpoints. The IPR 
& Exploitation Manager supported by the Communication & Dissemination Manager will have holistic view of the 
innovations arising out of the project, and will advise individual partners on IPR and funding strategy, with the aim of 
maximizing the commercial potential of the innovations created. IP ownership will belong by default to the partner’s 
creating it, and will be subject to terms and conditions outlined in the Consortium Agreeme nt. The Innovation & 
Exploitation Manager will update the Project Coordinator of the innovations arising, and recommendations for next 
steps on how best to handle it. In relation to decision making, the IC will decide on all matters with regard to IPR and 
exploitation, whereby each beneficiary can decide how best to protect and own its own IP, and joint IP will be decided 
by the beneficiaries involved, with each beneficiary in this case being assigned a vote (and decisions being taken by 
simple majority). The IC will have the ability to take decisions that relate to the implementation of the WP7, but any 
strategic decision such as those in relation to IPRs that affect the consortium, etc. will be raised to the PSC for voting. 
Moreover, in meetings of the PSC, the IPR & Exploitation Manager on behalf of the IC will report on the status of 
Innovation Management Activities.  
Appropriateness to the complexity and scale of the project 
This organisational structure is considered appr opriate for the management of this project, in view of its size, 
multidisciplinary nature and its S&T scope and ambition, and its expected innovation impacts. With key roles and 
responsibilities, each body within the structure ensures that there is dedicated and qualified management and skills-
sets mobilised at the different levels, as opposed to a centralised, one -dimensional management approach, which 
would be highly unlikely to deliver the necessary versatility. To this end, there is an integral approach  to the 
management of the project, ensuring:  
• effective management of the day-to-day running of the project & its resources, appropriate interfacing with the 
EC (Project Coordinator) 
• all participants have a stake in the strategic management of the project (Project Steering Committee) 
• effective management of the execution of the interdisciplinary work plan and its ability to deliver impact, 
whereby 2 executive-level Committees have been planned : the Scientific &  Technical Committee will be 
responsible for ensuring the project achieves its research objectives through sound management of the overall 
S&T work and it s potential risks; the Innovation Committee will be responsible for effective dissemination and 
management of the knowledge and data generated, IPRs, as well as other innovation-related activities required 
to deliver market exploitable results and to map out further research in order to build on the project results.

Innovation management  
A key objective of publicly-funded research is that it should lead to the exploitation of results, which goes one step 
further th an the mere production and dissemination of new scientific knowledge 117. As described , our project 
envisages an Innovation Committee and an IPR & Exploitation Manager in its organisation structure and we also have 
a dedicated Task 7.7. Innovation and IPR Management, which will be closely linked with the IP and Knowledge 
Management work in Ta sk 7.8 Exploitation of results and Business model develo pment. Our IPR & Exploitation 
Manager, Cristina Barragan, has the necessary entrepreneurial spirit to foment the conditions for an innovation eco-
system to flourish. She has a deep business understanding, along with a strong technical background for ensuri ng 
creative ideas are anchored to the required market, regulatory and performance requirements. In addition to IP 
protection, our Innovation Management activities will pivot around the implementation of an innovation cycle, which 
is a vital component for ensuring success in market-oriented research projects. Close interaction with the S&TC will 
be promoted to facilitate co-creation and fluid interaction between the development teams and our industry en d-
users. Open brainstorming, idea management, and the fact that WP1 will contribute to a deep understanding of the 
market needs, industry constraints and regulatory/standards framework  at the outset of the project for further 
activities to build upon. Thereafter, and in particular through WP2-3-4, the processes will be selected based on their 
capability to be upscaled to produce the new materials in sufficient amounts for WP5 whereby validation for ours 
end users case studies will be performed. The market s trive will accompany the entire work plan and the 
development teams will be guided by feedback loops from fellow developers, end-users and market insights to fuel 
an innovation cycle that leads to exploitable project results for a successful project outcom e in terms of innovation 
impacts. In addition to the mar ket drive of the technical development, we are in fact embedding our innovation 
strategy in a quadruple innovation helix model by contextualizing it within number of inputs from/ and outcome to 
the ‘natural environments of society’ as well as ‘media-based and culture-based public’ and ‘civil society’ by involving 
interactions with governmental/policy makers as well 
as stakeholder s including consumers again 
contributing to a multiplying effect for our innovation 
potential and impact (fig. 3.2). The Circular Plastics  
Helix also provide s an open innovation 
environment to generate new collaborations. 
Critical risks and mitigation measures 
Risks can be categorised as follows; technology related risks, market related risks and transversal risks (environment 
related risks and organisation related risks) 118. Technical risks will be managed by the Scientific & Technical 
Committee. Market-related risks and environment related risks will be closely analysed by the Innovation Committee, 
and organisational -related risks will be managed by the Project Coordinator supported by the Project Steering 
Committee and will be embedded in the close monitor ing of the evolution of the work. Table 3.2b shows the main 
risks identified to date, their probability of occurrence, the severity of the problem (impact), the actions to mitigate 
the risk and foreseen contingency actions. Through Task 8.2, a continuous p rocess of risk identification and 
management (of risks below and any newly identified risks) will be implemented based upon the principles and 
guidelines of the FERMA (ISO 31000 related) Standard 119. Agreement sought for risk -related contingency actions 
from the S&TC (in relation to technical risks) and the IC (in relation to market- and environment-related risks) will be 
taken by the PSC.

3.3  Consortium as a whole  
Bringing together public and private organisations across Europe  and involving cooperation among actors in the 
supply chain, from producer to final consumer, and from rese arch to policy makers  is key for the interdisciplinary 
approach needed for Circular Economy based innovation. The Preserve consortium is made up of 26 partners from 
9 countries: 8 EU countries (Belgium, Spain, Germany, France, Czech Republic, Italy, Netherlands, UK, Slovenia), as 
well as a Germany-based European association with significant policy outreach capacity. We have an integrative 
consortium covering a broad geography and including from small Eastern EU-firms to world leading blue-chip Global 
corporates. Our team constitutes a pan-European eco-system that unites the necessary infrastructure, knowledge, 
expertise, services and industry value chain to succeed in delivering on the project’s objectives to realise the expected 
impacts of the topic CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 - Upcycling Bio Plastics of food and drinks packaging.  
As illustrated in fig. 3.3, the consortium brings together comprehensive interdisciplinary pockets of knowledge. There 
is solid scientific presence  covering all relevant fields (AIMPLAS, FR AUNHOFER, CTB , ASU, UNIBO, ITENE, NTT ), 
combined with strong industrial and commercial involvement (10 SMEs including an industry association and 9 large 
enterprises) to ensure that the value chain of commercial actors can progress swiftly towards the intr oduction of 
new viable circular bio -based packaging solutions. RTOs will work closely with technology and service providing 
companies ( OWS, PLATO, IRIS , DENIMX), polymer , coatings and adhesive  producers ( BOSTIK/ARKEMA, BIOPOL), 
compounder specialised in recyclable plastics (PLANET, CARB), packaging manufacturer (SUDPACK, GPI, SIBO), end 
users (Danone, MDLZ, BDF), recyclers/upcyclers (SILON, ROMEI), as well as the largest biopolymer association EUBP. 
To strengthen impact, complementary partners have been included in terms of transversal activities and to ensure a 
business-driven and market-focussed approach to the project: innovation  and exploitation planning , IPR & Data 
management (KNEIA), Dissemination (CHX/ EUBP). In short, this is a complete storyboard of actors. 
Importantly the consortium will draw on the voluntary and 
objective advice, exper tise and support of External 
Stakeholders Group (ESG ), in order to complement the 
consortium’s industrial and technical insight in relevant fields. 
ESG members inclu de CocaCola, Manor Farm, Pack4Food, 
FlandersFood, PackCluster, CEFLEX, IVLV, ZLV, and more to be 
liaise with during the project . Each will provide invaluable 
insights into different applications that could use bio -based 
materials or that could use SRM, or could act as strategic 
adopters obtaining a license for the developed technologies.  
As a condition to generate growth, this is an industry-oriented 
project. It is coordinated by the highly experienced technology 
SME, IRIS, and a number of the WP leaders a re also from 
industry. The industry participants have been instrumental in 
helping to shape this proposal, and Preserve is considered a 
highly strat egic for assisting them in gaining a competitive 
edge and in being a pioneering group in driving forward 
Circular Economy-enabled innovations in the field of plastics. 
Each industry participant will be able to grow their businesses 
and improve their competitiveness in line with their position on the value chain. Fig. 3.3, where partners are clustered 
according to their positioning on the supply and value chain, shows how each partner is relevant and complementary.  
Finally, in relation to the gender dimension of our consortium, our team of researchers, technologists, industrialists, 
business experts, and policy influencers has a good participation of females. A number of the key management and 
decision-making positions within the project organisational structure have been assigned to highly qualified women, 
not least the roles of the Project Coordinator (Dr. Elodie Bugnicourt) and the IPR & Exploitation Manager (Dr. Cristina 
Barragan), as well as number of WP and task leadership roles. Interestingly, females are among the key drivers of 
this proposal (Elodie Bugnicourt, Jana Kadlecová, Esra Kucukpinar, Lorena Rodríguez, Isabel De Schrijver, Patrizia 
Cinelli, Sophie Macedo, Kristina Eißenberger, Annamaria Celli, Lola Gómez, etc.). Recommendations regarding 
recruitment for securing future researchers and development profiles for the project will be overseen by the Project 
Coordinator in WP8 to ensure a reasonable level of balance between the sexes (gender balances will be considered 
as a selection criterion between equally qualified candidates).

3.4  Resources to be committed 
The project budget has been built using a bottom-up methodology. There is a logical budget distribution among the 
partners and each has mobilised the necessary staff/person months (Table 3.4a) and infrastructure to get the job 
done in a competitive timeframe. The necessary personnel resources reflect the realistic efforts required to deliver 
the project objectives, and have been costed up based on actual costs for staff for each partner organisation (in line 
with average staff costs within the sectors and r eflected the differences in cost of living between the different 
participating EU regions). Equipment costs included in the project are for depreciation only. A reasonable budget has 
been allocated to mobility of developers and industrialists between sites, which is important for knowledge exchange 
and building excellence among multidisciplinary and international teams, as we ll as for practical on -site testings 
across partners as needed. Minimal subcontracting costs have been budgeted as the consortium has the internal 
resources and knowledge to perform the work.  
The OG&S (OG&S) that need to be contracted have also been included (and a breakdown of these costs are provided 
in Table 3.4b (for partners whose Other costs exceed 15% of personnel costs).The SMEs and industry partners occupy 
a sufficient portion of the budget ( 36% of the EC contribution goes to SMEs , 27% to large  companies and 37% to 
RT0s), ensuring a practical research-industry partnership for high competitive impact. There is an appropriate budget 
allocated to communication , dissemination, IP and knowledge management and business planning activities . 
Considering th at there are 26 partners in the project, and a competitive 48-month work plan that will output 
knowledge, upscaled processes, a pilot recycling plant for enzymatic delamination-enabled by biopolymer coatings 
and at least 10 demonstrators of different packaging formats including films, trays, liquid containers, textiles and 
composite from virgin bioplastics and SRM s as well as combining them with paper and board, for packing food, 
beverages, personal care and generic transport of products, resulting in mater ials with high transferability to other 
industries, a requested EC Contribution below 8M€ is very good value for high impact.

4.1. Participants (applicants) 
 
Participant no. 1 Name (shortname)/ Country IRIS Technology Solutions S.L (IRIS) / Spain 
Description of the legal entity  
  
IRIS Technology Group (http://www.iristechnologygroup.com/) is an advanced engineering Group that was 
established in Barcelona in 2007. IRIS Technology Solutions S.L, located in Barcelona, specialises in the manufacture 
and integration of Process Analytical Technology (PAT)-based real-time quality monitoring solutions for the process 
industries and IoT systems for smart manufacturing, predominantly targeted at the food, pharmaceutical and 
chemical industries. In particular, our product line comprises proprietary state-of-the-art IR analysers for at-line and 
in-line process monitoring.  
On the one hand, our solutions are based on the latest developments in photonics in the fields of MEMs, Near 
Infrared Spectroscopy, Hyperspectral Imaging, and Raman. On the other hand, we leverage ICTs, whereby we apply 
Machine learning, Artificial Intelligence and Data Mining techniques for predictive and active control, as well as for 
decision support systems. In addition to photonics -based analysers, we also work with IoT se nsors for enabling 
equipment and machinery for smart manufacturing and transitioning industry to the Industry4.0 paradigm. Our 
solutions are cloud-based for mobility, remote monitoring and multi-site applications.  
Our Innovation Division which is governed  by an Innovation Committee comprising Senior Management, and an 
Innovation Unit for managing and executing the company’s innovation roadmap, has 3 core strategic lines, for 
shaping the Factory of the Future: 
1. New optical photonics-based technologies and PAT systems for production process optimization 
2. ICTs (Artificial intelligence / machine learning, IOT & cloud platforms) 
3. Circular and Bio-based Economy: digitalization and waste valorization 
In addition to running an internal R&D programme, as well as carrying our various joint private projects with industry 
partners, our Innovation Division is highly experienced in working in collaborative R&D projects in H2020 (both as 
coordinators and partners), principally in  the SPIRE, FoF, and BBI programmes. The company was established in 
2007 and currently employs 60+ staff with a turnover of € 5 M. It is equipped with engineering workshops (3), food 
testing and wet chemistry laboratory, optics labs (2), and an electronics /telecommunications lab. IRIS is ISO 
9001:2008 certified and also is certified under UNE -EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems R&D&i. We are also 
certified by the local (Catalonian) government as a provider of technological R&D services (Tecnio Certification).  
IRIS is a member of the following sectorial networks: SPIRE, SPIE and SECPHO, in addition to regional industrial 
collectives such as Smart Space (association of companies and organisations that specialise in the ‘smartification’ 
of industry). 
Main tasks 
Using its core photonic competences, IRIS will have a strong role in terms of developing the right approach for 
demonstrating the sorting ability of the new materials developed in the project (WP4), in terms of process 
monitoring for the materials m orphologies obtained via self -reinforcement and for the control of the coatings 
application/ microplastics release  (WP2, 3, 5). In WP5, they will  support the food packaging validation trials by 
comparative shelf life assessments. In WP6, they will develop a DST to support the selection of the optimal upcycling 
route by the stakeholders. In WP7, they will also contribute in terms of IPR, innovation and knowledge transfer and 
training activities. Finally, IRIS will act as Project Coordinators (WP8) and they have extensive expertise at this level, 
and in particular in the context of industry-driven FP7 and H2020 projects, and private contacts with the industry. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
IRIS has a matrix of multidisciplinary knowledge groups in the company with strong expertise in engineering and 
science. With its team and resources, including electronics, mechatronics, mechanical, optical, industrial design 
engineers, as well as speciali sts in system engineering, application programming and web development etc., IRIS 
can carry out full system design and engineering, including electronic design and assembly, firmware and software 
development, electrical harnesses and interconnections, mech anical design for enclosure and prototype 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 3 of 68 
integration, as well as installation, validation and industrialisation of prototypes and equipment in production 
plants. In addition to this broad cross-disciplinary engineering team, IRIS’ research team consists of data scientists, 
chemiometricians, chemists and physicists, among others, who have the expertise to validate the technologies 
developed, with specific insights in biopolymers and their use in packaging.

Dr. Ing. ELODIE BUGNICOURT. (female) Masters in Material Science & Engineering (2002), PhD in Polymers and

Participant no. 2 Name (shortname)/ Country Albstadt-Sigmaringen University (ASU), Germany 
Description of the legal entity  
 
Food technology & nutrition is the core part of the education programme and the applied research in the faculty of 
Life Sciences of Albstadt -Sigmaringen University. Its activities belong to food product & process innovation (e.g. 
research projects in optimisation of food processing, functional & nutritional properties of food and food packaging) 
and production of cosmetic products with botanical extracts. Business innovation modelling is also a central part in 
the faculty of Business Science & Management of ASU. Advanced materials are the core research and teaching field 
for the faculty of Engineering. Within the faculty of Life Sciences, new sustainable packaging concepts are the 
research focus of the newly founded Sustainable Packaging Institute (SPI). The SPI delves into research and teaching 
in the area of biogenic raw materials, process technology and process design, functional materials, smart packaging, 
preservation and packaging as well as bioeconomy and sustainability. ASU is a project partner in the  field of 
safeguarding food quality & sustainable food packaging and in the field of developing new business models. It aims 
to expose students & scientific staff to real world problems in an EU-scale, thus enabling them to interact with other 
skilled actors in an international environment. 
Main tasks 
ASU will support in WP1 to define the specifications for the Preserve solutions to be developed. Moreover, ASU will 
contribute to WP2 regarding the development, processing and testing of combinations of proteins/ PHA coatings 
and adhesives (together with I VV) and FA grafting technologies. In this WP, ASU will also give input regarding the 
development and characterisation of films with tailored structures and barrier properties. In WP3, ASU lead the lab 
scale set-up of eBeam treatment for selected materials and blends. This will include the characterisation of the 
treated materials regarding mechanical, barrier (WVP/OTR), optical (colour) and chemical (degree of crosslinking) 
properties. As results from WP2 and WP3 feed in WP5, ASU will also be involved in this WP and will support in the 
coating scale-up and the trials with moulded pulp. Additionally, ASU will take the lead for the consumer perception 
and acceptance studies conducted in WP7. 
ASU act as project scientific and technical manager. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
At ASU the faculty of Life Sciences scientific staff is very experienced in the development and characterisation of 
food and food packaging. This includes the surface modification of bio -based films as well as the incorporation of 
active packaging constituents and the full characterisation of packaging relevant properties. They can perform 
sensory testing of food contact materials with respect to their interactive processes and compliance with food 
regulation. The faculty of life sciences has the intense know-how about degradation reactions of food during storage 
trials.

CENTRE SCIENTIFIQUE & TECHNIQUE DE L'INDUSTRIE 
TEXTILE BELGE (CTB) / Belgium 
Description of the legal entity  
  
CTB is the Belgian scientific and technical centre for the textile industry, a membership organisation with strong 
links to the majority of the textile and plastic conversion companies. C TB offers a complete range of standardized 
testing, it is a notified bod y for protective clothing, is also involved in standardization committees and offers 
technological advice and training to companies in Belgium or abroad. Via take-over of the “Flemish Plastic Centre” 
its expertise and services have been diversified towards the plastic and composite industry. 
The research focus of C TB is on applied research, funded by private contract as well as national and international 
agencies (e.g. H2020, FP7, LIFE, Interreg, Eranet). 
Some well selected subjects for strategic research are: (i) extrusion processes and related polymer formulation (incl. 
biopolymers); (ii) intelligent textiles; (iii) textile reinforced composites: (iv) innovative finishing, coating and 
laminating formulations and technology; (v) implementation of nanotechnology and (vi) additive manufacturing. 
In the past decennium la rge expertise was built -up in the domain of processing via formulation and pilot line 
processing of a range of biopolymers including PLA, PBS, PHA and biopolymer blends. This resulted in a range of 
industrial implementations in different domains. 
CTB has also a large expertise in plastic recycling and has the necessary equipment available to test the recyclability 
of different polymer materials, including packaging foils. 
Main tasks 
CTB will have important tasks in WP3 (Upcycling of core materials and blends), WP4 (Biodegradation, compostability 
and materials recycling) and WP5 (Upscaling and Validation of upcycled packaging, textiles and composites from 
primary and secondary raw materials). PHA coatings will also be developed by Centexbel in WP2. 
The main tasks therefore include:  
a. Processing of biopolymers into foils, injection moulded pieced, monofilament & multifilament yarns at 
lab and pilot scale and evaluation of the properties 
b. Application of PHA coatings 
c. Evaluation of reprocessability recycled PLA materials. 
d. Develop recycled bioplastics with improved properties through self -reinforcement and the formation 
of microfibrillar structures 
e. Evaluation of chain extenders and compatibilizers to improve the reprocessing of polymer blends 
f. Upscaling the reprocessing of monomaterials and self-reinforcement from biomaterials 
g. Supporting the end user companies in material evaluation for specific products, perform first validation 
trials to produce first demonstrators 
Furthermore, CTB will give input in the req uirements for packaging products (WP1) and support exploitation and 
dissemination tasks (WP7). 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
CTB, as a technologic centre, is focused to help companies in the textile sector & plastics converting industry to 
develop new materials & products and increase their competitiveness through innovation. CTB is already for several 
years working on recycling of  polymers and on the processing of biopolymers to support the industry in the 
transformation towards innovative and sustainable textile products and preparing the shift towards a sustainable 
bioeconomy. 
CTB has state-of-the art test facilities for chemical, physical, microbiological and burning behaviour testing, as well 
as pilot lines for extrusion, injection molding, coating, knitting & braiding, weaving. This equipment is used for 
research projects and direct evaluation of new material & technology possibilities by a variety of companies.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical e quipment, relevant to the

CTB has a fully equipped testing and processing lab available with all the relevant machines. Specific for processing: 
twin screw compounders, extrusion line, injection moulding machines, compression moulding, therm oforming,.. 
starting from lab scale up to pilot scale machines. New investments in purification machines (extraction, mixing, 
better processing,..) are done recently creating an open innovation platform on circular economy. More specific 
following equipment is available: 
• Micro-compounder & twin-screw compounder under water pelletizer for formulating biopolymers. 
• Lab lines for small scale testing of formulations (10 à 200g) in mono- & multifilaments 
• Pilot line for tape & monofilament production; mono - and bi component structures, pilot lines for 
multifilament yarn production: FDY, POY, BCF; mono and bicomponent (throughput 2 -14kg/hour, 
production speed up to 3500 m/min) 
• Semi-industrial injection moulding machines, profile and sheet extrusion line (width 50 cm), blown film 
extrusion line 
• An IR dyeing machine offers the versatility to test up to 16 different formulations in one run. For further 
upscaling CTB has a lab scale reel and a roll-to-roll semi-industrial coating and padding equipment. 
• Knitting, weaving, braiding equipment 
• All relevant analytical instruments to characterize polymer properties including, rheological behaviour, 
stability, thermal properties and morphology, mechanical properties of textiles and plastics

CONEXAS (AIMPLAS)/ Spain 
Description of the legal entity  
 
AIMPLAS, Technological Institute of Plastics located in Valencia, is a private, non-profit Association with more than 
650 associated companies created in 1990. AIMPLAS is formed by +170 highly skilled professional, more than 65% 
with a Masters, Engineering  or equivalent degree in Chemistry, polymer engineering, materials engineering or 
equivalent, including 22 PhD.  
AIMPLAS’ fields of work are related to technological research and development on thermoplastic and 
thermosetting plastic materials & products, its transformation processes and their recyclability and sustainability. 
AIMPLAS generates new knowledge and technologies that can be transferred to companies in order to help them 
to increase their effectiveness and competitiveness. 
AIMPLAS has a broad expertise in the fields of recycling, compatibilization, reactive extrusion, biopolymers and 
renewable source materials, special assisted processing technologies and nanocomposites, gained during the last 
years in the frame of EU and na tional projects. Nowadays, AIMPLAS has participated in 100 EU projects in FP5, 
FP6, FP7, LIFE+, CIP -EcoInnovation, H2020, among others, coordinating more 40 of them. In H2020, AIMPLAS is 
participating in more than 20 projects, coordinating most of them. Ou tstanding LIFE projects were celebrated at 
the Green Awards ceremony in Brussels on 30 May 2017, BREAD4PLA – with AIMPLAS as a coordinator - was 
honoured as one of the two most exceptional LIFE projects of the programme's 25 -year history. At National and 
Regional levels AIMPLAS participates in around 100 projects yearly. 
Main tasks 
AIMPLAS will lead WP2 and will mainly be involved in the production of PHA coatings, its application by different 
printing methodologies according to the proposed demonstrators , as well as its characterisation (oxygen and

AIMPLAS, as RO is focused to help companies in the plastic sector to develop new products and increase their

polymer/plastics/composites production technologies present in the industry nowadays and has state -of-the art 
test facilities for chemical, optical, morphological, mechanical and physical characterisation. These pilot lines and 
laboratories are used by many customer’s every year allowing them  to test new materials, optimize production 
processes and launch new products to the market, supported by AIMPLAS technical staff, resulting in more than 
5000 assays, 170 technical assessments and 120 training actions to more than 1500 clients per year. 
AIMPLAS has 9,000 m2 state-of-the-art facilities, including thermoplastics and thermoset pilot plants, analysis and 
testing laboratories (physical-mechanical, chemical, packaging, automotive and construction) and training areas. 
AIMPLAS is member of several international networks and organisations, such as ECP4, AESICOM or BIC and 
standardisation committees (ISO and CEN).
