FRAUNHOFER GESELLSCHAFT ZUR FOERDERUNG DER 
ANGEWANDTEN FORSCHUNG E.V. (IVV) / Germany 
Description of the legal entity  
  
 
 
The Fraunhofer Gesellschaft zur Förderung der angewandten Forschung e.V. is the 
leading organisation for applied research in Europe, undertaking contract research 
on behalf of industry, the service sector and the government. Within the framework 
of EU technology programs, they are actively involved in industrial consortia which 
seek technical solutions to improve the  competitiveness of European industry. An 
annual turnover of about 2.3 billion € is generated in contract research by about 
28,000 employees in 74 research facilities and institutes. 
In December 2017, the Fraunhofer -Gesellschaft was awarded the Logo »HR Ex cellence in Research« from the 
European Commission in recognition of its outstanding Integrated Human Resources Management. The Logo »HR 
Excellence in Research« is based on the 40 principles of the European Charter for Researchers and the Code of 
Conduct for the Recruitment of Researchers (»EU-Charta & Code«). As Europe’s leading organization for applied 
research and as project partner many EU-projects, Fraunhofer fulfils these principles. Fraunhofer is one of the first 
organizations for applied research in Germany to receive the Logo. 
The Fraunhofer Institut für Verfahrenstechnik und Verpackung (Fraunhofer-Institute for Process Engineering and 
Packaging, IVV) in Freising, Germany has approx. 300 employees and an annual turnover of €23.9 million. The 
activities comprise development of products and processes primarily in the area of food ingredients, food 
development, functional packaging materials, product safety, food quality, biogenic raw materials as well as 
plastics recycling. The scientific department ‘M aterials Development’, of Fraunhofer IVV will be involved in the 
tasks of the proposal. 
The department ‘Materials Development’ focuses on development of improved and alternative packaging 
materials and packaging solutions. Their research focuses on production of polymer films by extrusion or coating 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 13 of 68 
substrates with barrier layers. Developments are aiming on material reduction, material substitution by 
sustainable alternatives and implementation of functionalities for active packaging. The department compris es 
processing of packaging films and demonstrators in pilot plant scale as well as testing laboratories. On pilot plant 
scale extrusion casting and coating, compounding, lacquering and metallization facilities are available. The 
adjacent laboratory is accredited according DAkkS D-PL-11140-04-00 for oxygen permeability (DIN 53380-3) and 
water vapour permeability (DIN 53 122 -1). Further characterisation techniques are mechanical testing, surface 
energy measurements and surface characterisation techniques (FTIR, AFM, SEM, Raman). 
Main tasks 
IVV will bring its expertise in development of biobased packaging materials and multilayer films in WP2 and WP5. 
They will participate in the development of protein-based coating formulations and respective adhesives in close 
cooperation with ASU and BOSTIK (WP2). Application of the coatings in pilot scale will be conducted using the pilot 
facilities at IVV. As barrier improvement is a key competence of IVV, they will establish a PVD process for inorganic 
barrier layers with protein coatings. IVV will support partners with characterisation of coatings, particularly barrier 
testing. In WP5, IVV will support SÜDPACK (WP5 leader) with production of multilayer materials at pilo t scale 
before upscaling to industrial size for consortium end-users (MONDELEZ, DANONE). 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
IVV has competence in products and processes primarily in the area of food ingredients, food developmen t, 
functional packaging materials, product safety, food quality, biogenic raw materials as well as plastics recycling, 
and is therefore well -suited for a multidisciplinary project like PRESERVE. The tasks will be mainly performed by 
the team of the ‘Materials Development’ department, but coordination across departments, e.g. Dpt. of biogenic 
raw materials, would allow addressing upcoming challenges during the project. IVV has a team of experienced 
scientists, engineers and technicians in different fields as  material science, chemistry, physics, process 
engineering, packaging engineering, and food science. At IVV there is a long-year experience in related projects in 
biopolymers and multilayer materials for food packaging.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the 
proposed work 
1. Compounding: A co-rotating twin screw-extruder (Dr. Collin, 24 D, 25 mm diameter) with feeds for powder, 
flakes and liquids is available for compounding the hot-melt adhesives.  
2. Extrusion: A 7-layer extrusion plant is used (Dr. Collin, nozzle width 300mm, film width up to 500mm, feed 
1-15 kg/h, film diameter 20 µm – 3mm, 4 different polymers simultaneously) for the production of multi-
layer film structures, the extrusion of single-layer films and the extrusion coating and extrusion lamination 
of film sheets. The film thickness is monitored in-line with a capacitive sensor.  
 
Figure 1. 7-layer extrusion plant at Fraunhofer-IVV for extrusion lamination of thermoplastic protein-based adhesives

3. Wet chemical coating: A wet chemical coating machine is available, which is unique in its possibilities of 
applying thin adhesive layers, in drying and curing, and in sensitively treating the barrier layers until 
lamination (50 cm roll width, 30m/min speed, up  to 140°C convection drying tunnel, corona -treatment, 
different application techniques gravure and slot-die, UV-curing) 
 
Figure 2. Wet-chemical coating pilot line at Fraunhofer-IVV for the coating of protein-based lacquers and wet chemical 
lamination of bio-based adhesives for packaging applications 
4. Inorganic barrier coatings : For physical vapour deposition (PVD) of inorganic barrier layers an electron -
beam vacuum coating unit is available. Film widths are 280mm, deposited species could be metals (Al) or 
metal oxides (Al2O3, SiOx).

energy (wetting angle), film thickness, FT-IR, DSC, AFM, Raman, SEM-EDX, optical microscopy.

Participant no. 6 Name (shortname)/ Country INSTITUTO TECNOLOGICO DEL EMBALAJE, 
TRANSPORTE Y LOGISTICA  (ITENE) / Spain 
Description of the legal entity  
 
ITENE is the specialist Technological Centre in R&D in packaging, logistics, transport and mobility. Its mission is to 
generate scientific and technological knowledge and adding value to companies through the implementation of 
R+D+I in these areas. ITENE provides business solutions with an integrated view of the supply chain, from raw 
materials, design and development of packaging and packaging systems, optimisation of the movement and 
distribution of goods, until the products reach the consumer and are ultimately managed as residues, all within a 
framework of sustainable performance. The centre has advanced facilities and a multidisciplinary team of 
researchers and technicians with proven and constantly evolving technologies for novel solutions. 
ITENE was founded in 1994 and currently employs 153 persons. Located in Valencia, Spain, the centre has 7,105m2 
of facilities covering laboratories and experimentation infrastructures equipped with the most modern 
technology. 
ITENE research area covers: 
• New Advanced Materials (Development strategies to obtain new packaging materials with better properties) 
• Functional surfaces and Intelligent Packaging.  
• Food safety and Active Packaging (Materials tha t release active substances from the packaging or absorb 
undesirable substances from the product to prolong the shelf life)   
• Packaging Technologies (vacuum, modified atmosphere) 
• Packaging Engineering (Transport simulation technologies) 
• Sustainability (Waste valorisation, LCA, LCC, Carbon Footprint) 
• Transport and Logistics (route optimization, distribution modelling, urban mobility) 
• Electronics, Robotics and Industry 4.0 
ITENE has participated in 39 projects from FP6 and FP7 and is involved in 25 H2020 projects (most of them under 
execution). 
Main tasks 
ITENE will act as task leader of those activities related to release of microplastics, circularity assessment and food 
safety and regulations. More specifically, ITENE will lead: 
Subtask 2.4.1. Optimization of the formulation of Functional Finishing treatment to reduce microplastics, where a 
coating and a finishing treatment will be developed and tested in order to reduce the release of microplastics.  
Subtask 2.5.2. Application of a functional finishing treatment to reduce microplastics., where Health and safety 
aspects and control of the release will be analysed.    
Task 6.4 Circularity assessments. ITENE will carry out an KPIs assessment to ensure circular approach of the project 
results  
Task 6.5 Identification and assessment of Legal, Regulatory, Ethical, Environmental, and H&S Requirements, 
leading both: evaluation of the legal framework regarding the risk assessment of the prototypes and compliance 
of the prototypes with EU Food Contact Materials regulations 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
The R&D areas that will be involved in this proposal are advanced materials, sustainability, nanosafety an d food 
safety. These areas, covered with 100 people from 5 different disciplines (chemical engineers, agronomy 
engineers, physicians, biologists, and environmental engineers).  
Our Nanosafety research group has wide experience in projects related with the risk assessment and management 
of engineered nanomaterials (ENMs) and release of ENMs in different compartments, including freshwater, soil, 
sediments and air. Moreover, the Nanosafety research group participates of the most important network of 
scientists related to the evaluation of the risk posed by the use of emerging chemicals, including the European 
NanoSafety Cluster and the Communities of Research in Nanosafety (CoRs) working groups.

The new advanced materials department provides expertise and new facilities to support the study and 
development of new materials in the nanometer range, including the design, synthesis and application of

from plastics contamination. ITENE is the  coordinator of this proj ect regarding Bio -based plastics

recycling more accessible, cost-effective and profitable for both citizens and professionals in the field.

project and working in the identification and optimization of enzymes, enzyme depolymerization, environmental 
assessment and validation.

design approaches in nanotechnology supply chains. ITENE is the coordinator 
6. LIFE ECOTEXNANO: Innovative tool to improve risk assessment and promote the safe use of nanomaterials in 
the textile finishing industry (Life+), ITENE worked in the health and safety impact for users and environment, 
including the release of microplastics. 
Description o f any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the 
proposed work 
The main facilities used in the project are the waste pre -treatment laboratory, the processing laboratory, the 
physical and chemical laboratory a nd the packaging and environment laboratory. The Pilot processing plant has 
several small and large equipment for extrusion, injection and compounding, pilot scaled reactors and a chemical 
and material laboratory to fully characterize the new products. The chemical laboratory of ITENE, coordinated by 
the new materials division, has the necessary equipment to characterize the NMs in powder or liquid form, 
including a transmission electron microscopy (TEM), scanning electron microscopy (SEM), z-sizers for DLS analysis, 
and TGA Q-5000 for Thermogravimetric analysis. 
• Processing laboratory: hydraulic press ASLAK, mini -extruder DSM Xplore and mini -injector DSM, twin 
screw extruder Brabender, twin screw compounder Coperion, cast line Dr. Collin (up to 5 layers), injection 
moulding machine Battenfeld, rotary coater machine (RK PrintCoat Instruments). 
• Physical and chemical laboratory: Liquid chromatographs coupled to different detectors (MS, PDA, UV-vis, 
LS, fluorescence), Thermogravimetric analyser (TGA) coupled to infrared (FTIR), Infrared Spectrometer 
(FTIR-Raman), Gas ch romatographs coupled to different detectors (MS, MS/MS, TOF, FID and TCD), 
Differential Scanning Calorimeter (DSC / MDSC) and Dynamic Mechanical Analyser (DMA), universal 
testing machine 
• Packaging and environment laboratory: Software of Life Cycle Analysis  SimaPro, Statgraphics and 
Multipack-Multimix. 
• Waste pre-treatment laboratory: magnetic separator for ferrous and nonferrous metals Goudsmit NF300, 
mill Retsch SM2000, shredder Blik B400, dryer Wittman Drymax D3050M.  
• Microbiological laboratory: Class II Laminar Flow Biological Safety Cabinet, incubators, autoclave.  Pilot 
Plant: Different capacity reactors and centrifuge 
The safety Research group has dedicated facilities and equipment to support the hazard, exposure assessment 
and characterisation of ENMS and ultrafine particles, including incubation chambers, high sensitive real time 
exposure monitoring devices for on-site exposure characterisation, and a new nano-aerosol exposure chamber

Description of the legal entity  
 
NTT is a private non-profit research company established in Prato since 1972. It has a staff of around 20 people, 
including employees and in-house consultants. NTT represents a reference point for research and technological 
innovation in the textile sector in Italy. The company is actively involved in research and demonstration projects 
on textile processing and textile machinery design realised at regional, national and European level. In particular, 
for the latter, NTT has participated in many projects fu nded by the LIFE programmes and the Framework 
Programmes concerning the textile sector and has also acted as coordinator of some of them. For instance, NTT 
has participated in seven projects of the 6th Framework Programme concerning the textile and clothing industry. 
Moreover, in the 7th Framework Programme NTT is involved in the following projects dealing with the application 
of textile in high added value application (i.e. energy production and personal protective equipment): NMP-2008-
SME-2-228439 (20010-2014) where photocatalytic materials were investigated; NMP-2007- 3.3-1-213903; FP7-
ENERGY-2010-FET-256736; where nanosized spacer has been produced. The key expertise of the company is 
distributed among different divisio ns. The proposed technical activities will mainly involve the Division of 
Chemical and Environmental Technologies, dealing with: chemical processing of textiles and nonwovens for 
apparel and technical applications; research and development of plasma, electron-beam, microwave, ultraviolet, 
laser and enzymatic processes; development of photocatalytic materials; textile analyses in its certified lab; 
assessment of environmental footprint of manufacturing sector by means of LCA. 
Main tasks 
- Involvement in WP3: Optimisation at pilot scale of prototypes radiation treatment by e-beam  
- Involvement in WP5: Implementation of ebeam treatment for upcycling   
- Leading WP6: Evaluation of the environmental, economic and social performances of the new products  
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
NTT has a huge experience on the production of nanomaterials (including both titanium dioxide nanop articles 
and nano-fibres and polymeric materials at micro – i.e. filament – and nano – i.e. functional nano-fibers, scale) 
exhibiting self -cleaning, antibacterial and antipollution properties. Furthermore, NTT is investigating the 
effectiveness of E-Beam for the production of composite and laminates with high impact resistance for aerospace 
and automotive applications and is recently deeply involved in promoting sustainability in the manufacturing 
sectors (in particular the textile industry) by investigatin g environmental performances of different 
manufacturing processes by means of LCA.

ALMA MATER STUDIORUM - UNIVERSITA DI BOLOGNA (UNIBO)/ 
Italy 
Description of the legal entity  
 
Founded in 1088, the Alma Mater Studiorum – Università di Bologna (UNIBO) is one of the most important 
institutions of higher education across Europe. Research and Innovation are a priority of the University mission. 
UNIBO has an active patent portfolio of over 370 patents, related to more than 140 inventions , set up or 
accredited 27 spin -off companies and can also count Almacube , as business incubator. With regard to the 
capability of attracting funding, UNIBO is very active both at National and European level. Activities related to 
competitive funding programs are supported by the Research and Third Mission Division, with more t han 10 
years’ experience and about 50 people assisting the research groups. A Research Support Office deals with the 
UNIBO strategic positioning at local, national and international level, through integrated networking and lobby 
activities. The Programs&Pr ojects Office supports the UNIBO researchers with technical, legal, financial and 
administrative expertise. Moreover, the Office cooperates with the Knowledge Transfer Office, for the Innovation 
Management expertise and the IP protection and exploitation. Thanks to its scientific excellence and a central 
Project Management support, UNIBO has gained a considerable experience in International and European 
research projects, successfully participated in FP7 with 274 projects funded in 2007-2013 (58 as coordinator) and 
87,8ML Euros of funding, UNIBO is the second Italian university for the attractiveness of European funding for 
research, 37th in the European ranking of institutions of higher education. In Horizon 2020, UNIBO is so far 
involved in 262 funded projects (69 as coordinator) with more than 105ML Euros of funding.  
UNIBO will participate to the project with the Industrial and Environmental Biotechnology and the Polymer Science 
groups of the Department of Civil, Chemical, Environmental and Materials Engineering (DICAM).  
The Industrial and Environmental Biotechnology group  has expertise in the development and optimization of 
biotechnological processes, either based on microbial or enzymatic biocatalysts, for the production of bio-based 
products, the biodegradation of low MW xenobiotics as well as of bio -based and petroleum-derived polymers. 
The group has also expertise in the isolation and characterisation of microorganisms from extreme environments 
and of their enzymes, and possesses a large collection of bacteria from desert, extreme environments. 
The Polymer Science group  has a wide experience in the development of new synthetic routes to produce 
biobased polymers and strategies to prepare advanced materials, such as nanocomposites, for packaging, coating 
and biomedical applications. Moreover, the group is expert in the characterisation of polymer properties. 
Main tasks 
Using its biotechnology and polymer chemistry competences, UNIBO will have a strong role in material recycling 
in WP4. In particular, UNIBO will employ commercial hydrolytic enzymes for the controlled biodegradation of 
polyesters such as PLA  in order to recover oligomers or monomer from such polyesters.  Subsequently the 
depolymerized products will be upcycled to obtain new biopolymers with enhanced functionalities t hrough 
chemical reactions with multifunctional monomers. The new materials obtained will be fully characterized and 
will be employed in WP2 in the application of new upcycled bioplastics (e.g. adhesives, coatings).   
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
Two research units of UNIBO belonging to DICAM department are involved in Preserve. The Biotechnology group 
has expertise in the development and optimization of enzymatic processes for the degradation of traditional and 
biobased polymers. The Polymer Scien ce group is expert in synthesis and characterisation of bio -based 
monomers, polymers and advanced materials. The group has a specific expertise in preparation of aromatic and 
aliphatic biobased polymers, starting from biomass and in the synthesis and modification of polymeric structures 
to get specific functionalities (i.e. antioxidant, antibacterial, barrier properties).

Participant no. 9 Name (shortname)/ Country BIOPOLIS SL (BIOPOL)/ Spain 
Description of the legal entity  
 
Biopolis, S.L. is a leading biotechnology company based in Valencia (Spain) active in new product development 
and applications. Created in October 2003, Biopolis is still owned directly by the Spanish National Research 
Council (CSIC). Biopolis shares are currently  distributed between the Spanish National Research Council (CSIC) 
and ADM Wild Valencia, S.A.U. The company is classified as large company.  Our core competences are the 
isolation, selection, design, characterisation, validation and production of microorgan isms and cellular 
metabolites with applications in agri-food, feed, pharmaceutical and chemical industries. This includes the design 
and development of microbial strains and metabolites, by strain and bioprocess development, followed by 
fermentation and downstream process optimization and the production at an industrial scale.  Biopolis, S.L. has 
also generated novel high -throughput screening platforms in vitro and in vivo, which enable us to evaluate and 
characterize the effect of selected ingredients in relation to nutritional and health protection functionalities. 
Therefore, the selected compounds can be produced and also evaluated in terms of their functional activity in 
the host.  Prototype projects in clude the selection, validation and production of starters and probiotics, the 
selection and production of enzymes, the identification, characterisation and process development of 
biochemicals and the design, validation and scale-up of novel bioprocesses. Patents and publications have been 
issued in relation to functional ingredients and probiotics and biopolymer production, including co-developments 
with our private and public partners.  Biopolis facilities spread over 1,500 m2 including laboratories and 
manufacturing plants, located in the Scientific Park of the University of Valencia. Our R&D centre hosts 9 
specialized research laboratories (biochemistry, molecular biology, cellular biology, microbiology, cell culture, 
chemistry, analytics, and bench-top and scale-up fermentation), a pilot fermentation and DSP unit (up to 300L) 
and an industrial plant with a total capacity of 9,000 L fermentation. The company cornerstone is a 
multidisciplinary staff, consisting of highly trained and specialized professional s in biology, biochemistry, 
biotechnology, organic chemistry, food technology, and industrial and chemical engineering. 
Main tasks 
The main role of Biopolis will be to upscale the fermentation of mcl-PHA in WP2 that will be as coating for several 
packaging formats.

production of different biotech solutions at an industrial scale.

Participant no. 10 Name (shortname)/ Country PLANET BIOPLASTICS SRL (PLANET) / Italy 
Description of the legal entity  
 
Planet Bioplastics (PLANET) is an innovative start -up, spin-off of the University of Pisa that includes among its 
owners two Professors of Pisa University. Other owners of the company have large experience in production and 
marketing of polymeric materials. The company has access to equipment for processing and characterisation in 
the University of Pisa and in the company Caldara, producer of recycled plastic compounds, whose owners are 
even partly owners of PLANET. PLANET is a full BIC member and partner of two European BBI-JU projects; PLANET 
plans to be involved in regional, national and European projects with high R&D participation but oriented to 
obtaining innovative products to propose on the market of bioplastics. PLANET is currently partner of two 
European BBI project ECOAT and BIONTOP.  
Thus, the company is strongly interested in the present project for production and marketing of biobased and 
recyclable products. As well the company as previous experience on material pre -treatment to improve 
recyclability and subsequent selection of compatibilizers and additives to improve properties of plastic produced 
using a percentage of recycled polymers.  
In the timeframe of the project the company plans to hire 1-2 persons that will be partly dedicated to the project. 
Main tasks 
PLANET will take care of pilot and industrial production of compounds to be used for production of items by 
injection moulding, cast extrusion and blow moulding extrusion.  
PLANET will contribute to set optimal conditions for detergent separation of multi-layers materials by protein or 
adhesive removal with water, solvent including enzymatic solvent on laboratory scale to be scaled to pilot-
industrial scale by the partner ROMEI.  
PLANET will contribute to optimize biobased polymers formulation with selection of chain extenders, nucleating 
agent and reinforcing fillers, and scale up compounds production.  
Processing conditions as thermal profile, screw configuration, feeding of additives etc. will be optimized by 
specific energy study. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
The managerial team, on the academic side, is composed of professors with strong scientific background on the 
properties and transformation of biopolymers (especially Polylactic acid and Polyhydroxyalkanoates) and with 
huge experience in National and Europ ean projects, carried out both as coordinators and RTO partners. The 
business side is composed of an expert marketing sales manager and three entrepreneurs, who own a company 
that carries out recycling and compounding of traditional plastic materials. They  have 55 years of specialization 
in the regeneration and trade of plastic materials, with the mission of reducing non-recoverable plastic waste to

Participant no. 11 Name (shortname)/ Country Bostik SA (BOSTIK) / France 
Description of the legal entity  
Bostik was founded as the Boston Blacking Company in Chelsea, 
Massachusetts, in 1889. For most of the 20th century as the company 
embarked on international expansion and diversification, specializing 
in producing different families of adhesives for differe nt markets and 
applications. In 1990, Bostik was acquired by the TOTAL group, and by 
Arkema in 2015. Today, Bostik, as a division of Arkema, is a global leading player in adhesive for the industrial, 
consumer and construction markets with over €2.0bn of tu rnover, about 6,000 employees and 4 major R&D 
Centres in France, USA, Japan and China. Bostik benefits of its mother company’s policy of investment in 
innovation: Arkema invests 3% of its revenue in R&D, filed 244 patents in 2018 and employs 1600 researche rs. 
Developing and producing adhesives requires dealing with several different chemistries such as polyamides, 
polyesters, polyurethanes, acrylics, polyolefins and styrene -block-copolymers among others. Bostik’s adhesives 
are applied in the form of hot mel ts, pressure sensitive hot melts, films, solvent -based coating, solvent -free 
coatings, waterborne and extrusion resins.  
In the global Packaging industry Bostik designs, produces and commercializes lamination adhesives, cold seal 
coatings, heat seal extrud able co -polyesters and lacquers. Bostik is also the pioneer and global leader in 
extrudable pressure-sensitive hot-melts for reclosable lidding films.  Bostik also supplies adhesives for tapes and 
labels, for case and carton sealing as well as paper-based consumer goods.  
Main tasks 
Bostik will be leading task 2.3, with the development of laminating adhesives and the subsequent production of 
the selected candidate formulations at laboratory or small pilot scale (> 10 L), to be used by partners in tasks 2.5 
for pilot scale lamination trials, and for the production of packaging laminate prototypes. Two different adhesive 
technologies will be explored: 
(a) two-component reactive adhesives for wet lamination, based on isocyanate prepolymers with a vegetable oil 
polyester backbone having more than 50% biobased content, designed to provide high adhesion to protein -
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 28 of 68 
coated biodegradable plastic substrates and peel strength exceeding the food packaging industry requirements 
at very low coating weights ca. 2-5 g/m². 
(b) a biodegradable hot melt adhesive based on casein suitably formulated with plasticizers and other plant-based 
proteins to be melt -processable at temperatures allowing extrusion lamination without damage to the 
biodegradable substrates. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
Bostik is a major producer of adhesives for the manufacture of flexible packaging laminates for food and non -
food products, with an experience of more than 40 years in the synthesis, production and application of various 
laminating adhesive technologies in cluding one - and two -component polyurethanes, solvent -based or 
solventless, for the lamination of all the plastic film substrates commonly used in food packaging. Bostik also 
produces hot-melt heat-seals, cold-seals and extrudable pressure sensitive adhesi ves for reclosable packages. 
Significant expertise is available in Bostik R&D centre in Venette (F) both in terms of polymer synthesis, 
formulation, application and analytical characterisation of the adhesives and the laminates produced. Bostik is 
equipped with state-of-the-art pilot scale laminating & coating equipment. Strong focus is given to anticipating 
customers’ needs in terms of performance, regulatory evolution, low cost -in-use, sustainability and innovation. 
Bostik is strongly committed to support  their customers packaging makers, brand owners and retailers with 
regards to innovations towards minimizing the environmental footprint of packaging.

Description of the legal entity  
 
Carbiolice (https://www.carbiolice.com/en/) is a start-up created in 2016 with the ambition to respond to one of 
the major environmental challenges of our decade: plastic pollution. Backed by the protection of some forty 
patents with an international coverage, Carbiolice has developed a unique, univ ersal and innovative solution in 
the form of an additive that makes biobased plastics compostable in domestic conditions and thus helps to fight 
plastic pollution through composting / organic recycling innovation is aimed at plastics and packaging applications 
which, by their nature, cannot be recycled. It is an innovative and eco -responsible alternative for achieving zero 
waste. The plastics thus designed can be assimilated to bio -waste, which will be a decisive element in the fight

against plastic pollution but also an effective and complementary lever for the deployment of an efficient solution 
for sorting waste at source. 
CARB is the fruit of the shared, complementary ambitions of Limagrain Ingredients, a global seed company, 
CARBIOS, a green chemistry company developing enzymatic technologies, and the investment fund SPI, managed 
by Bpifrance. They have more than 15 years old experience in bio -polymers and industrial applications. They are

Main tasks

composting internal tests before transferring samples to i.e. OWS.

Participant no. 13 Name (shortname)/ Country SÜDPACK VERPACKUNGEN GMBH & CO.KG 
(SUDPACK) / Germany 
Description of the legal entity  
 
The Südpack Packaging Group is one of the leading manufacturers of co -extruded soft and rigid films, flexible 
plastic laminates and vacuum bags in Europe. One focus is on printing films using flexographic and rotogravure 
printing processes as well as digital printing. The main markets of the packaging manufacturer with headquarters 
in Ochsenhausen are meat and sausage products, fish, dairy products, bakery products, but also pet food and 
technical articles (non -food, medicine). Today, the Südpack Group manufactures in  five countries worldwide 
(Germany, Switzerland, France, Poland, USA) and sells its products in 73 countries. In 2017, the company had 
around 1350 employees and achieved sales of over 379 mio €.  
The company was founded in 1964 and is still family -owned, actual in the second generation. It was one of the 
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 32 of 68 
first to develop plastic bags that enable controlled gas exchange and thus became a specialist for cheese maturing 
bags. The company grew steadily and opened its first foreign branches in the UK and Switzerland at the end of the 
1980s. In 1988 the subsidiary Ecoform was founded. In 2002 the company Piciotti in Bioggio, Switzerland, was 
taken over. Today, the gravure printing process competence centre is located there. Four years later, Südpack 
opened its customer centre for film development. Today, the Südpack Group focuses, among other things, on the 
area of coextrusion of high -barrier films. Special attention is paid to the development of high -performance, thin 
materials that help to save resources and thus  protect the environment. CDP Laboratories was founded in the 
north of France in 1989. After a long and close cooperation, the company was integrated into Südpack Medica in 
2005, which had been founded two years earlier. One focus of the company is the pro duction of medical sterile 
packaging in clean rooms.  
The film manufacturer's product portfolio ranges from multi -layer hard and soft films, tubular bag films and top 
films to convenience solutions for the microwave and prefabricated pouches. In addition, the company prints its 
films in-house in gravure printing with up to twelve colours and in high-quality flexo printing with up to ten colours. 
Südpack adheres to the highest hygiene and quality standards, which is reflected, for example, in certification 
according to ISO 9001 (1994), production according to HACCP guidelines (1996) and certification according to 
BRC/IOP (2003). With the help of the environmental management system according to ISO 14001 introduced in 
2009, work is being carried out on the con tinuous improvement of the resource, waste and energy balance. The 
in-house development centre offers the possibility of testing new packaging materials on various packaging 
machines. These include thermoforming machines, tray sealers, vertical and horizontal form fill and seal machines.  
Main tasks

furthermore be responsible for cast-extrusion (r-bioPET) and blow-extrusion processes of biopolymers (r-PLA and 
r-bioPE).  
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
SUDPACK is a leading provider of film packaging across Europe and therefore an important partner to bring the 
material concepts on the way to industrial maturity. They will build the bridge between packaging developments 
at TRL5 (conducted by RTOs IVV, AIMPLAS and CTB) and the end users (MDLZ, DANONE, BDF). As a specialized 
company for flexible multilayer packaging production, t heir R&D activities are related to all kinds of flexible 
packaging (food and medical), plastics processing (cast and blow film extrusion, thermoforming) and coating and 
printing techniques. They already have PLA based solutions, as well as packaging from recycled resources in their 
portfolio.

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the 
proposed work 
1. Cast extrusion: The pilot plant “multiXtrusion” offers all kinds of necessary plastic extrusion techniques for 
flexibles. Mono- and multilayer cast films can be produced as cast films at high speed, with high control of 
the properties and independent from the production processes of the main plant, at film widths up to 
600mm. Cast extrusion is feasib le for film thicknesses > 20µm, so also for sheet production of 
thermoformable trays 
2. Blown film: For production of thin films with very even surface, even with the possibility of combination to 
multi-layer film structures during the production process, the blown-film pilot plant will be used. The film 
properties achieved by this process allow deposition of inorganic barrier layers. 
3. Coating / lamination / printing : All three processes will be demonstrated on an in -line pilot plant (flexo 
printing and coating). The processes can be run on soft films (e.g. for pouches), hard films (for trays) or 
cardboard < 300g/m2.  
4. Application technology centre:  
Extensive packaging and production tests can be realized in the application technology centre, such as 
thermoforming of trays, sealing tests of pouches or packing-specific mechanical testing (e.g. T-peel testing).

Main tasks

How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
BDF uses plastic, glass, metal, cardboard or paper in products packaging to reduce material use while maintaining 
stability and quality. This yields more than just economic benefits. Every stage of the packaging life -cycle offers 
potential savings that can make a substantial contribution to environmental protection. This includes low-energy 
production technologies, reduced transportation, and waste minimization. Since 2009, sustainability has been 
strategically anchored in cosmetic packaging development processes. The goal is to apply the sustainability criteria 
of "avoid, reduce, reuse and recycle" to all of packaging innovations. To identify the reduction of the environmental 
impact of packaging, Beiersdorf use s Life-Cycle Analyses. These help the company to understand how resource -

Description of any significant infrastructure and/or any major items of technical equipment, relevant to the 
proposed work 
Infrastructure for: 
-Methods, technologies and test designs to demonstrate the effectiveness of cosmetic products. 
-Bulk compatibility test 
-Determining the compatibility and stability of existing or new packaging (e.g. new geometry, new packaging 
materials such as plastic resins, etc.) in correlation with existing, new formulations or new formula technologies. 
The test method comprises testing:  
1) The material compatibility and stability of a packaging system in correlation with an existing or new 
formula technology (new base formula). Hereby the formula is organoleptic checked as to its properties 
and the new packaging system is visually checked as to its properties.  
2) Weight loss in%. 
3) Light stability. 
4) Perfume testing. 
5) The packaging system regarding appearance and function. Comparison with sufficient reference samples 
as control for bulk compatibility and perfume stability is required. For details please refer to standard 
ancol stability test.

List of up to 5 relevant publications, and/or products, services (including widely -used datasets or software), or 
other achievements relevant to the call content 
Relevant solutions: 
1. DRY CLEANING: cleaning without water. At the heart of our innovative mechanical dry-cleaning technology is 
a high-speed centrifuge. Acceleration and impact forces inside the centrifuge cause paper to break down and 
contaminations to be spun off from plastics. Not a drop of water is used in this process, allowing to save money 
on water supply and wastewater management. In addition, the waste volume is reduced by at least 50%, which 
is especially important given the ever-rising cost of waste disposal. 
2. HYDRO POWER WASHING: The first cleaning phase for the plastic waste begins with the Friction Washer, which 
uses a large volume of circulating water in a constant cycle. This gives the contaminations a good soaking and 
makes it easier to remove during the second cleaning phase. The high -intensity washer then gives the pre -
washed plastics a thorough, final cleaning. The contaminations are removed by means of powerful frict ion 
between the screen basket and the rotors in the centrifuge. The force applied by the cleaning system is strong 
enough to remove even difficult dirt. No additional water is required during this phase and the plastic is 
dewatered alongside the cleaning process 
3. MECHANICAL DRYING: High peripheral speeds are needed to spin water from these surfaces. The extra -long 
Pla.to rotor optimises drying efficiency by allowing the film particles to remain inside the dryer for an especially 
long time. The machine also h as an integrated fan in a wear -resistant design that generates a powerful air 
flow. The fan sucks the film through the machine while also taking up the evaporating water. At the same time, 
residual debris is removed from the surfaces through friction. The cleaning system automatically removes dirt 
particles together with the spun off water from the dryer. 
4. THERMAL DRYING: Pla.to Thermal Dryers achieve outstanding drying results by applying hot air to the wet 
plastic in a highly intensive process. The machine surfaces are thermally insulated to minimise heat losses. 
5. DENSITY SEPARATION WITH THE HYDROCYCLONE: the process guarantees a precise separation for a greater 
product quality.  
This proposal version was submitted by Elodie BUGNICOURT on 14/05/2020 16:20:41 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Funding & Tenders Portal Submission System.
              CE-BIOTEC-09-2020 
Page 46 of 68 
6. ZIG-ZAG ASPIRATOR: The most common example is the removal of labels from PET bottles. The thick PET flakes 
need to be collected, while the  labels need to go. The Zig -Zag Aspirator uses an air flow to suck up the 
lightweight labels. The heavier plastic pieces fall to the bottom. Another advantage is that the shredded 
material is dust free, which is a huge gain in further processing

Romei company is specialized in post -industrial plastic scraps recycling. The company was established in 1983

(flakes and  granules). It can efficiently supply many markets from the goods manufacturing sector to the 
packaging industry. The investments on quality standards allows us to offer recycled products with similar 
characteristics as virgin products but with a lower price and the minimal carbon footprint.

Description of the legal entity  
 
DenimX B.V.  (www.denimx.nl) is a development and production company of products, made out of recycled 
textiles. After more than 5 years of research and development under the flag of industrial design studio MMD, 
DenimX was officially founded as a company in February 2017 and is located in Maastricht, The Netherlands. Its 
main aim is to add value to discarded waste streams and create good -looking, functional and commercially 
feasible products in large volumes by combining textile fibers with bio-based binders into a re-usable, recyclable 
composite material. DenimX’s businessmodel consists of 3 pillars:  
1. Consultancy of large SME’s and multinationals regarding their sustainability policy within the field of 
development, production and material usage 
2. Design, engineering and production of upcycled products that are sold by affiliated distribution partners 
per market segment (i.e. furniture, lighting, acoustics and carpets market) 
3. Design, engineering and product ion of an upcycled product collection that is sold directly to B2B 
customers or to end consumers, using an online shop and direct sales 
DenimX has several larger companies and organizations as a client e.g. Nike Europe, DSM Dyneema, Dutch 
Ministry of Defense, Elis, PI (Penitentiary Institution) and City of Maastricht, yet functions as a hub and director 
of development and production processes. The company is founded and run by Marc Meijers, industrial designer 
with over 25 years of practical experience in product development. He is momentarily DenimX’s sole owner and 
‘employee’. For every single project a team is composed that fits the request.  
Main tasks 
DenimX will have a strong role in the creation and development of technological and commercially viab le 
solutions for upcycling of discarded materials, with a focus on, but not limited to textile composites with bio -
based polymers SRM (WP5). DenimX will add know-how of various materials and production technologies and a 
vast network of production and finishing partners and will add creative input to the process.  They will also test 
the DSS from WP6.

Participant no. 
 23 Name (shortname)/ Country Silon s. r. o. (SILON)/ Czech Republic 
Description of the legal entity  
 
Silon s. r. o. is a recycled PET staple fiber producer and compounder located in the Czech republic celebrating 70 
years of existence in 2020. The portfolio ( www.silon.eu) includes compounded PE, PP and PA material of various 
types and recycled PET fibers, produced as a staple or tow. The main areas of the target market include automotive 
sector, civil engineering, cable industry, hygiene and food packaging. The company is IATF 16949, ISO 9000, ISO 
14000 certified. 
The compounds division features wide range of expertise related to compounding of powders (talc, CaCO3), glass 
fiber, glass beads, carbon fiber and cross -linking modification of polyolefines. As well the laboratory is equipped 
with wide range of analysers including a unique chlorine-testing device for water pipe assessment. The production 
premises operate under the strict HACCP or GMP principles. The compounding is done on single-screw and twin-
screw extrusion lines with either cut filament chip forming or sphe rical chips. The material can be packed in 
protective or standard packaging, based on the sensitivity. 
In the Fibres division, Silon has one of the longest expertise in PETbottle flakes recycling for over 20 years of such 
production. Silon is supplying wid e range of automotive and hygiene products made of rPET, with standards 
quality, guaranteed by Öko-tex certificate Class I, for some of the assortments fulfilling the FDA regulation. Most 
of the production is performed on a single step fiber line of different type, both with single-screw and twin-screw 
extruder. The raw material is dosed either via crystallizer to improve the properties of the PET flakes or via the IR 
dryer. 
The fiber division can produce 3.0dtex to 17 dtex staple fibre cut length 38 to 85 mm. 
Main tasks 
Silon, as an industrial member of the consortium, is mainly aimed at the practical validation of the project results. 
It means the main task is a successful reprocessing of recycled materials for textile purposes and for further pre-
processing for packaging and films on an industrial level and the specifics, that may be related to such 
reprocessing, as well as technology related specifics, adjustments needed to deal with the recycled raw material 
of different origin. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
Due to the fact that recycled fiber production is a niche type of plastics processing, Silon has used its lasting know-
how and expertise and developed many unique solutions in past that has positive impact on the processability and 
stability of the material produced. As well in the compounding division there is a wide know-how due to the variety 
of materials in the portfolio, with very different applications and needs. 
Both divisions feature very skilled specialists in textile analyses, polymer science of both types, recycled material 
and the specifics and virgin material, and related equipment for raw material chemical analyses (chromatography, 
NIR, FTIR analyses; viscosimeters etc) and mechanical lab for both fine materials as fine dtex fibre and polymer 
testing bars.

Participant no. 25 Name (shortname)/ Country CROWDHELIX LIMITED (CHX) /UK 
Description of the legal entity  
 
The Crowdhelix Network (CHX) is a pan -European Open Innovation Network that enables Research Technology 
Organisations (RTOs) and businesses to collaborate, innovate and grow. The Crowdhelix Network has more than 
450 member organisations from 44 countries and is present in all EU Member State countries. The network 
membership is reported to have won more than €4.5 billion of funding under Horizon 2020, highlighting the 
quality of its membership base. The network is structured around virtual technology clusters known as He lixes. 
There are currently 21 live Helixes in areas such as Digital, Health and Energy etc. The network hosts focused 
collaborative events for each Helix each year where the aim is to connect organisations across Europe and 
promote collaboration and open i nnovation. In addition to hosting and running events, CHX also has its own 
technology tool called: Crowdhelix. The tool is designed so people and organisations can profile their expertise 
and capabilities within a Helix area. It is then used to help organi sations post opportunities, which are matched 
to people’s profiles within the platform. Once a match is made, the CHX team helps to facilitate an opportunity, 
so that it then turns into a tangible collaboration. 
Main tasks 
In WP7, Crowdhelix will help PRESERVE address parts of the impact section by managing the stakeholder 
engagement and clustering activities. It will leverage and expand the Circular Plastics Helix - a virtual community 
of experts in recycling, circularity and renewable-sourced plastics. Launched in the frame of the ongoing project 
MultiCycle, the Helix acts as the communication and knowledge exchange platform for the project. It will include 
all partners, relevant stakeholders from the Crowdhelix Network, aligned projects, an d any other actors with 
interest in plastics and the circular economy. The purpose of the Helix is to 1) increase the visibility of the project 
and promote its activities findings among the users of the Crowdhelix platform, 2) provide central online space 
for knowledge building and advancement of innovation, 3) create a sense of community and inclusion among 
experts working in the fields of plastics and sustainability. Crowdhelix will also lead clustering activities and ensure 
PRESERVE is networked with other projects in the area of plastics circularity. Building on the legacy of the Plastics 
Circularity Multiplier initiative and other relevant networks, Crowdhelix will promote cross cooperation between 
EU projects and initiatives and work to boost the impact of the project in a resourceful way 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
With 450 member organisations in 44 countries, Crowdhelix is uniquely placed to disseminate the key message 
of the project across the research and innovation landscape. Its pan-European community currently has a reach 
to over 500,00 individuals representing research centres, universities, and industries. The network connects 
excellent researchers and innovative businesses and enables them to collaborate, innovate and grow. The Circular 
Plastics Helix service will be to lead on activities related to stakeholder engagement and clustering. More 
fundamentally, the Helix will profile and inject relevant commercial actors from across Europe, such as SMEs and 
Industry leaders commercialising in this space, with a view to forging alliances and partnerships that are in the 
spirit of growth, expansion and ongoing sustainability and advancement of the IP created beyond the end of the 
project. The Helix will also identif y relevant and appropriate open source communities with a view to ensuring 
that open outputs from the project are made available and accessible to all EU SMEs, RTOs, universities and 
industry actors, in the spirit of open dissemination and sharing. CHX wil l continue to manage the community 
beyond the end of the project – promoting the project’s outputs and impacts and enabling new forms of 
collaboration and open innovation across the European Research Area.

Participant no. 26 Name (shortname)/ Country EUROPEAN BIOPLASTICS EV 
(EUBP)/Germany 
Description of the legal entity  
 
 
European Bioplastics (EUBP) is the industry association representing the bioplastics industry in Europe across the 
entire bioplastics value chain. Established over 20 years ago, EUBP now has 70 member companies from across 
the globe. EUBP’s members primarily produce, refine, and distribute bioplastics, i.e. plastics that are bio -based, 
biodegradable, or both. In addition, biomass feedstock producers, bioplastics converters and compounders, and 
several renowned academic and private research institutions are also members of EUBP. The association’s key 
objectives are to serve as a contact and network platform, as a primary resource for information about the 
bioplastics industry, and as a catalyst for advancing the objectives of the growing bioplastics industry as a whole. 
EUBP coordinates various working groups (WG) and product groups (PG) focused on these themes, such as the 
PG Bio-based, PG Biodegradables, the WG Regulatory Affairs, and the WG Communications, and actively supports 
the introduction (e.g. CEN TC  249 and 411) and monitoring (e.g. EN 13432) of industry standards and best 
practices. As part of that commitment, EUBP has introduced the Seedling® logo, an EN 13432 -based conformity 
mark of industrial compostability for biodegradable plastic packaging. I ncreasingly, EUBP comments on political 
processes linked to the advancement of the Circular Economy and the Bioeconomy in Europe and legislation 
impacting on the bioplastics industry’s ability to fully bring to bear its innovative potential. 
Main tasks 
EUBP will primarily contribute to the definition of specifications for the upcycled bio -based packaging (WP1) 
according to c consumer and market requirements that are well known through its member organizations. 
Furthermore, EUBP will help to shape the speci fications for materials and processes and support PRESERVE by 
input covering legislative aspects for bio-based materials. 
Along its core mission, covering the provision of required biopolymers -based solutions along the value chain, 
EUBP will lead communication and dissemination (WP7), by reaching out to consumers, scientific and industrial 
community members by several educational and dissemination events, that will help raising public and societal 
environmental awareness and policy outreach to encourage the adoption of PRESERVE’s new bio-based solutions 
and flanking existing and upcoming EU policy strategies, such as Plastics Strategy, CEAP and Green Deal. 
How the legal entity profile matches the tasks in the project 
EUBP is registered as an association in Germany, classifies as an SME, and is membership-based. EUBP currently 
has <10 employees who represent a very broad range of expertise and backgrounds, ranging from polymer 
chemistry, to economics, to political and social science, to seasoned communication and PR specialists. This mix 
of different and relevant expertise, the international network groomed over decades, a nd the range of subjects 
covered by EUBP staff in their daily operations render EUBP a suitable partner for this project.

5. Ethics and security
5.1 Ethics 
 
During the preparation of this proposal, in keeping with the required Ethics Appraisal Procedure, an Ethics Self-
assessment was performed with the completion of the Ethical Issues Table, and this project does not involve 
Ethics issues. 
Nevertheless, ethic aspects will be overseen in the  subtask regarding RRI in WP8 and other aspects like the 
respect of GDPR, e.g. in the dissemination activities or for the consumer perceptions assessments , will be well 
accounted for in WP8. Furthermore, ethical aspects related to the developed products will be considered in the 
s-LCA in WP7. 
All in all, the ethical footprint of th e project will be very positive vs. the current situation by: i) reducing the 
depletion of finite resources, ii) limiting leakage in the environment or impact thereof, iii) limiting food waste.
5.2 Security3 
 
In terms of security, project will involve NO: 
• activities or results raising security issues 
• 'EU-classified information' as background or results 
 
  
 
3 See a rticle 37 of the Model Grant Agreement. . For more information on the classification of Information, please refer to the Horizon 2020 guidance: 
https://ec.europa.eu/research/participants/data/ref/h2020/other/hi/secur/h2020-hi-guide-classif_en.pdf.

ANNEX: Support letters from External Stakeholders Group 
 
Summary of current External Stakeholders Group members and respective roles (more members will be added during 
project implementation based on needs and cross-fertilisation potentials): 
 
Name (Short name) Type Country Role 
CocaCola Large Germany Definition of the requirements for biopackaging for other 
beverage products and formats, provide feedback on 
developed packaging and early adopter when available 
Manor Farm Large Ireland Manor is interested to use bio -based materials for meat 
packaging, and therefore could be interested also in the 
project outcomes. 
PackCluster Association Spain PackCluster is interested in interacting with us in order to 
define the current issue with packaging circularity and 
collaborate in cross dissemination activities 
Industry Association for Food 
Technology and Packaging 
(IVLV) 
Association Germany Access food packers aspirations and concerns in terms of 
recyclability of packaging materials and use of biobased 
materials  
FlandersFood cluster 
organisation 
Belgium Flanders' FOOD is a unique, strategy -driven platform that 
contributes through innovation to a more competitive, 
innovative and sustainable agri-food industry. 
Zentrum für Lebensmittel und 
Verpackungstechnologie e.V. 
(ZLV) 
Association Germany Diffuse best practices to food packers in terms of use of 
biobased and recycled materials  
Pack4Food Cluster 
organisation 
Belgium Pack4Food is a consortium of 45 companies, the most 
important Flemish research centr es active in the food -
packaging interaction field and network organizations. 
Pack4Food aims to stimulate innovation in food-packaging, 
both at the food producer and at their suppliers (packaging 
producers, filling machine producers, ...), and also to 
support companies in their everyday packaging challenges.  
CEFLEX- A circular economy for 
flexible packaging 
Industry-wide 
initiative 
EU CEFLEX is interested to follow new initiatives that can 
improve circularity of flexible packaging, therefore to guide 
us and benefit from the new knowledge generated
